Important News

Pinghan Railway Line 61

Situation of Fierce Fighting in Recent Days 62

Yu Xuezhong personally oversees the battle at Fangshun Bridge

Jin Army successively occupies Shizhuang and Zhengding

Deputy Commander's Headquarters establishes a battlefield emergency relief association

Baoding Correspondence: The war on the front lines has been extremely fierce in recent days. After the various units of the Northeast Army's Second Group Army reached their destinations, they have formed a large encirclement around Shijiazhuang. The battle formations and recent developments of both sides are briefly described below:

Fierce Fighting on the Left Wing: Since the Northeast Army's First Group Army lured Shi Yousan's troops to their destination, they were preparing to launch a fierce attack. However, Shi's troops suddenly disappeared, and they could not be found for two or three days. Spies and reconnaissance planes made several trips to investigate, but to no avail. Yu Xuezhong, Commander of the First Army, in order to wait for the various routes of the Second Army to reach their destinations, so that they could launch a simultaneous attack, specially ordered his subordinates to stand in strict formation and wait. Until the morning of the 29th, Shi's special brigade was suddenly discovered in the Xiaoligezhuang and Zhangdengzhen areas east of the railway, attacking the defense area of Dong Yingbin's troops of the Northeast Army's left wing. Because of this attack by Shi's troops, the Northeast Army learned that the main forces of Shi Yousan, Sun Guangqian, Shen Ke, Wang Xinde, and Zhang Xitian were all east of the railway line. Therefore, the 18th Brigade on the front of the railway line was also moved east of the railway line to cooperate with the units of Chen Guanqun and Dong Yingbin to intercept them. The front of the railway line was taken over by the newly arrived Heilongjiang Grand Mixed Brigade. From the 29th to the morning of the 30th, the artillery fire in the Zhangdengzhen, Ranzhuang, and Xiaoligezhuang areas was the fiercest. Shi's troops launched repeated fierce attacks, but were all repelled. On the evening of the 30th, Yu Xuezhong specially sent staff members Fang Huating and Zhao Yong to the front to inspect everything.

Bombing of Ranzhuang: On the morning of the 30th, a report was received stating that Shi's troops were all hiding in Ranzhuang village. Chen Honglu, Captain of the Aviation Corps, dispatched seven planes to bomb Ranzhuang in the morning. Ranzhuang is surrounded by water on all sides, and the village is full of houses. The planes bombed in teams simultaneously, first bombing the southwest corner, then the west corner, and then the southeast corner. Many of Shi's infantry were killed in the bombings. Finally, four bombs were dropped on a grove in the northeast corner. Shi's artillerymen then pulled out four or five gun carriages and fled out of the west gate. The rest that were damaged were abandoned in the grove. The planes pursued them to outside the west gate and dropped four or five more bombs, and Shi's troops fled.

Deployment for General Offensive: The battles east of the railway line in recent days can be described as fierce, but they are still local battles. The formal general offensive is still waiting for the encirclement to be fully deployed. As of the 31st, the various units of the Second Army had reached their destinations. The Second Army's formation is as follows: the 20th Brigade's Chang Jingwu's troops are stationed in Gaoyang, forming a link with the First Army at Zhangdengzhen. The 15th Brigade's Yao Dongfan's troops and Huang Shiyue's Brigade crossed the Henan border and advanced to Gaoyang. The 1st Cavalry Brigade's Guo Xipeng, in coordination with the 2nd Cavalry Division, arrived in Raoyang, preparing to advance towards Zhengding and Xinle, cutting off the retreat of Shi Yousan's troops.

Yu Personally Oversees the Battle: Yu Xuezhong, Commander of the First Army, believed that the deployment of all routes had been completed and that a general offensive could be launched simultaneously. For the convenience of command, Yu specially ordered all personnel in the unit at 4:00 AM on the 31st to prepare to personally set out to oversee the battle. The Adjutant's Office prepared Yu's special train. By about 9:00 AM, all personnel had completed their preparations. Only one section chief and two or three staff members were left in each department of the Baoding Military Headquarters to work in Baoding. The rest accompanied Yu. Yu boarded the train at 11:00 AM and set off for Fangshun Bridge. The military headquarters will advance forward with the army. When Yu left, he told people at the station that the Northeast First and Second Armies had been linked up, and the Central Army and the Jin Army were also advancing forward. Tonight or tomorrow morning, the encircling forces from all routes will launch a simultaneous general offensive. Shi is already surrounded on all sides. A clear victory or defeat can be determined within three days after the general offensive. (July 31st)

The Jin Army is Dispatched: Taiyuan Correspondence: Since the Shi troops problem arose, rumors about the Jin faction have been rampant, and the price of Jin currency has plummeted to $3.80. After the joint telegram of the North China generals was issued, the rumors subsided. Unexpectedly, the news that Xu Yongchang had returned to Taiyuan spread, and rumors arose again for a time. According to our investigation, the attitudes of the various generals are extremely clear. After Xu returned to Taiyuan, the generals held a banquet at the Zhengtai Hotel to welcome him back. During the banquet, they discussed sending troops to punish Shi. It was faintly heard that during the negotiations, although some people argued that Shi Yousan's forces were weak and that the Northeast and Central Armies could easily resolve the situation with a pincer attack from the north and south, the majority advocated that the Jin Army should, on the one hand, make contact with Sun and Pang's troops to prevent Shi's troops from collapsing and fleeing to Shanxi, and on the other hand, mobilize a large force to attack its rear and flanks from Niangzi Pass, in order to quickly end the military situation. It was decided that Shang Zhen would be the commanding general, because Shang had received a telegram from the Central Government a few days ago, ordering him to lead his troops out of Niangzi Pass. After receiving the order, Shang made considerable preparations and transferred a large sum of money from the Finance Reorganization Office and the Opium Suppression Office for use by the brigades of Gao Hongwen and Huang Guanghua under his command. After Shang set off, the provincial chairman was replaced by Qiu Zengyi. As for the issue of military pay, Shanxi Province is really unable to raise funds again and will be subsidized by the Central Government and the Deputy Commander's Headquarters. As soon as Fu Shuangying arrives in Taiyuan, there will be concrete measures. It is also heard that in addition to telegraphing Shang Zhen to lead his troops to attack Shi Yousan, the Central Government also telegraphed Gao Guizi and Pang Bingxun to lead their troops and join Shang's troops in attacking.

On July 30th, Shang Zhen transferred the Jin Army out of Niangzi Pass. On August 1st, the General Staff Office of the Army telegraphed Pingjin (Beiping and Tianjin) to report the dispatch of troops and the occupation of Shizhuang and Zhengding. The telegram stated, "Limited to immediate arrival, Shi's rebel forces are causing chaos and destroying unity. Our Army Commander Shang Zhen, in accordance with the telegram order of General and Deputy Commander Jiang and Zhang, dispatched troops to Shizhuang to attack the enemy's flanks. On July 30th, Gao Hongwen's brigade stationed in Meijing, JIngxing, Hengshui, and Shouyang, and Huang Guanghua's brigade stationed in Jingxing. On the morning of the 31st at 4:00 AM, Gao's brigade advanced to Huolu. After getting off the train, they selected 400 brave men and advanced towards Shizhuang. The entire brigade advanced in two columns. After arriving at the line of Daguo Village and Zhentou, they repelled the enemy's advancing troops and then approached the enemy's Currency Yuan area west of Shizhuang. The enemy's troops, about two regiments, resisted stubbornly. After two hours of fierce fighting, the enemy's forces were unsustainable, and Shizhuang was completely occupied at 10:00 AM on the 31st. Most of the remaining enemies retreated towards Zhengding, and a part fled eastward. More than 30 enemies were captured, along with dozens of rifles. Huang Guanghua's brigade advanced eastward into Shizhuang at noon and ordered Gao's brigade to pursue them closely. The enemies relied on the dangerous terrain on the north bank of the Hutuo River to resist. After three hours of fierce fighting, the remaining enemies were finally defeated and fled northeast. Gao's brigade then occupied Zhengding at 5:00 PM on the evening of the 31st. After being intercepted by our army, Shi's rebels were cut off at both ends, and knowing that their general situation was gone, their morale was scattered, and they were unable to fight again. They withdrew the main force from the Wangdu area and fled eastward. Our Gao's brigade, in addition to leaving a part stationed in Zhengding, still pursued them. One regiment of Huang's brigade was dispatched to join forces in attacking in the direction of Wuji. Army Commander Shang Zhen is temporarily stationed in Shijiazhuang and is waiting for orders to advance. Our northern and southern armies are also pursuing and annihilating the chief culprit, and the time is not far off. Special telegram reported, General Staff Office of the 32nd Army, Dong."

Battlefield Emergency Relief: Beiping News: Deputy Commander Zhang believes that the war is about to end and that the disaster victims in the war zone are displaced and in urgent need of relief. He has instructed the staff of the Deputy Commander's Headquarters of the Army, Navy, and Air Force to organize a Battlefield Emergency Relief Committee. Secretary-General Wang of the Headquarters, after receiving the instructions, immediately asked Zhu Guangmu to invite Qian Junren, of the Beiping Office of the Relief Committee, to the Headquarters to discuss organizational matters. After receiving the telegram, Qian immediately went. According to Qian, "Secretary-General Wang and Director Zhu invited me (Qian himself) to the Headquarters to discuss battlefield emergency relief matters and asked for my help, which is my duty. After two consultations, a general decision has been made. The relief supplies are divided into two categories: relief funds and relief grain, both of which will be planned by the Headquarters. Personnel will be dispatched to various war zones within days to conduct investigations. After the investigation, relief will be provided separately according to the situation, in order to show condolences. The committee has decided to set up its headquarters in Baoding and will go there to organize it within days. Only an office will be set up in Beiping, inside the Headquarters. As for the organization of the committee, I have drafted the articles of association and submitted them to the Headquarters. As soon as they are approved, they can be implemented." The Headquarters also announced, "We have just received instructions from the Deputy Commander that the Headquarters will organize a Battlefield Emergency Relief Association, which will be established within two days. It has been decided to transport large quantities of rice and flour and funds for military use to the war zone. First, reception centers will be set up, and then investigations will be conducted into the losses suffered by the people due to the war, and compensation will be made as appropriate, and condolences will be given to the wounded and dead. A large number of personnel have been transferred from various departments and will depart for various places immediately to handle matters separately in conjunction with local military, police, party, and government personnel and local organizations." (August 2nd)

Field Notes on the Korean Incident (Continued) 63

Essential Hopes of Overseas Chinese: After this unprecedented catastrophe, the overseas Chinese are extremely worried that the Koreans will commit a second act of violence. Those who have no property or family ties have packed up their businesses and returned home to take refuge temporarily. When there is an opportunity in the future, they will reside there again and revive their businesses. Those who have real estate and movable property that cannot be disposed of immediately are eager to sell them off or find someone to take over. Before leaving Korea, they earnestly hope that their compatriots in China will follow a proper path for anti-Japanese and anti-Korean movements and must avoid direct conflicts and using retaliatory measures, so that the overseas Chinese will not be sacrificed needlessly again. On this point, the overseas Chinese in Pyongyang and Gyeongseong have repeatedly pleaded with the reporter to convey this to China. Recently, when the anti-foreign goods movement occurred in China, overseas Chinese merchants in Korea encountered equivalent boycotts by Japanese and Koreans. If there are no unrestrained actions in China, the Japanese and Koreans may not dare to engage in illegal actions against our overseas Chinese again. Although overseas Chinese merchants have suffered losses, they are all determined to persevere, but the situation is difficult, and the Chinese people should understand this. Since the Korean Incident occurred, the government has only sent Minister Wang Rongbao to Korea to investigate and has not sent any special envoys to express condolences. In the future, what the overseas Chinese urgently want to discuss with the central government is that the consulates stationed there have lost the trust of the general overseas Chinese population. They are unwilling to consult with them on any matter. We do not know the reason for this. Recently, the Zhenhai warship of the First Fleet of the Northeast Navy, representing the government, went to Incheon and Zhennampo to express condolences to the overseas Chinese. Although the overseas Chinese in various places did not receive any practical benefits, the concept of the motherland has been particularly deepened. At present, the number of casualties and losses in various places is only being determined by the chambers of commerce in various places, without a systematic investigation. There is no legal basis, and the exact number of losses cannot be determined. The consulates have only reported to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs in a perfunctory manner and have not conducted any on-the-ground investigations or taken any measures to provide relief, which is enough to disappoint hundreds of thousands of overseas Chinese.

A General Overview of Japan's Management of Korea: Japan's management of Korea, viewed from a flat perspective, is benevolent and guiding; viewed from a three-dimensional perspective, it is high-handed and severe. It fundamentally divides the Korean people into several different groups. For the elderly, it allows them to live in peace and enjoy themselves. It not only does not destroy the old Korean etiquette and customs but also promotes them. It allows them to follow their social customs and does not suppress them as long as they do not harm public welfare and hygiene, so that the general remnants of the Three Han kingdoms enjoy a life of peace and prosperity and no longer think of Shu. For the young people, it uses specially formulated educational methods to educate them separately, subtly transforming them and causing them to forget their origins and the concept of the motherland, and automatically regard themselves as being on par with the Japanese. They wear Japanese clothing and speak Japanese, know nothing of Korea, and do their best to eliminate their pro-China thoughts and educate them that Japan and Korea were originally one race. Therefore, the emerging Koreans have a lighter concept of the motherland, and their anti-China actions are becoming increasingly fierce. As for the overall construction of Korea, Japan sets up what is beneficial to Japan itself. What is not related to Japan but is needed by the Korean people, Japan generally does not promote. Throughout the eight provinces of Korea, as far as the reporter has seen, there are virtually no projects purely created by the Korean people. That is, in Huangzhou in Hwanghae Province and Zhennampo in South Pyongan Province, sericulture, beekeeping, cotton cultivation, and fruit cultivation are all managed by the Japanese. They all implement new methods. The Koreans who raise silkworms and plant mulberry trees using old methods have lost their ability to compete and are gradually decreasing. In Japan, primary education for children is compulsory. In Korea, however, it is left to nature, and the Japanese government does not interfere with whether or not children of school age attend school. Therefore, the streets are filled with playful children. However, when Korean children need to study, they are not allowed to establish their own academies or organize any schools as a group. They must attend Japanese government schools. Important workers in factories are not Korean. When necessary, the Japanese will summon Japanese from their own country to fill the positions or replace them with Chinese, but they will not allow Koreans to participate. Therefore, the Koreans have remained ignorant and dull for the past twenty years. At the same time, the Koreans' laziness is evident everywhere. Judging from the actions of the general public, it is even more evident that they deserve the misfortune of losing their country. On the way from Pyongyang to Zhennampo, the reporter saw a Korean who looked like a farmer enter and sit in a second-class carriage. A Japanese policeman, who was a ticket inspector, saw him and asked for his ticket. He replied that he had not bought one and was asked why he had not bought one, but he remained silent. He was ordered to sit in a third-class carriage and buy a ticket, but he still did not speak. He was driven off the train, but he did not move. It was not until the Japanese became angry and summoned their comrades, who grabbed him and dragged him away, that he hurriedly took out money to buy a ticket. This also shows one aspect of his servility. There are only two Korean newspapers in all of Korea (not including those run by the Japanese). One is the Chosun Ilbo, which is controlled by the Governor-General's Office, and the other is the Dong-A Ilbo, which, although its attitude is relatively moderate, is often punished with suspension. Although there are occasionally magazines and other publications run by Koreans, they all have a Japanese background or are supervised from the side. Korean knowledge is simple, and there is no such thing as thought. The independence parties that call out overseas are just a few knowledgeable people. Judging from the domestic situation in Korea, not to mention the strict precautions of the Japanese army, even if it were not, it would be difficult for these people to restore their country and recover their lost territory. Heavy Japanese troops are stationed in Gyeongseong, Pyongyang, and Sinuiju. It is said that there are about 70,000 artillery and infantry troops. There is also an air force stationed in Pyongyang. Airplanes take off in the air every day, nominally for training, but in reality, it is nothing less than a warning to the Koreans not to have any illusions. Incheon is a port for both commercial and military use. The sea mouth is eighteen feet deep. Ships with deeper drafts must enter specially built docks to dock. Three sides of the dock are walled with stones, and three gates are set up. When the tide rises, the water is closed in the dock, and the average depth is thirty-five feet, so large ships can still be anchored alongside. Zhennampo is the base of the Second Fleet of the Japanese Navy. The two mountains on either side of the port face each other and have a commanding position. The Second Fleet has four ships that are permanently docked. The internal and external defenses are very strict.

The Journey from Liaoning to Andong: The Anfeng Railway from Liaoning to Andong is 550 li long. The South Manchuria Railway express train departs from Liaoning at 3:25 PM and arrives in Andong at 9:00 PM. The section from Liaoning to Benxihu is a double track, while the section from Benxihu to Andong is a single track. After passing Sujiatun, the mountains rise and fall continuously until Benxihu. The barren mountains, except for moss, are completely bare and without a single blade of grass or tree. The river forks are winding, and the water is mixed with mud and sand, turbid, shallow, and narrow, making it unusable. Most of the farmland is cultivated on the mountain foothills, scattered and broken, without half an acre of flat land. The saying in Guizhou, "People have no three fen of silver, and the land has no three chi of level ground," can be applied to this area. However, the mountains are mostly granite, and the faults are loose and easy to dig, and lime fossils and the like can be obtained everywhere. If we take advantage of local conditions, fossil mines and lime mines can be opened. The coal, iron, and limestone mines in Benxihu are one example of what the Japanese have established. Above Benxihu, there are overlapping mountains and swamps, and the forests and grasslands are endless. The farmland is becoming increasingly scarce, and the houses are mostly built against the mountains, and there are many stone houses. Three or five households can be found every few tens of miles. The population density is as sparse as in northern Manchuria. Except for the railway, it is impossible to see where the paths are. Residents who have not lived there for a long time already find transportation extremely difficult. The towns passed, such as Sujiatun, Lianshanguan, Jiguan Mountain, Wulongbei, and Fenghuangcheng, are relatively well-known, but the desolation of the markets is no different from the countryside. The supply of materials, apart from imports from Japan and the sale of foreign goods, is limited to coarse cloth for domestic goods. The Anfeng Line is built in the Wanshan Mountains, tunneling through mountains and building bridges over streams. The track is tortuous and often meanders through slopes and valleys. There are more than 30 bridges and tunnels, and the scale of the project is several times that of the main line of the South Manchuria Railway. The places passed, such as Motianling and Jiguan Mountain, are all natural barriers on the east side, with a shape that can be defended by one man against ten thousand. The Japanese have built extremely strong forts in all of these places, and other places can also be defended. It is a pity that this kind of dangerous place has already been occupied by the Japanese. Looking at what we see, we cannot help but sigh. Andong is the southeastern gateway to Liaoning. The Anfeng Road connects from Korea, like an arm reaching in, breaking through the gateway and reaching the hall. Although there are dangers such as Yuanshan Mountain and Zhengjiang Mountain facing each other, it is equal to nothing. The reporter took a round trip on the Anfeng Line. The passengers I rode with, except for a group of three who were Chinese, were all Japanese, either merchants returning home from the mainland or people from their country coming to the Northeast for inspection. They were bustling and busy. Being among them, we felt like we were sitting on pins and needles. Andong used to be a large city, with merchants gathering and markets thriving. Shahezi was especially prosperous. Due to the repeated anti-China actions in Korea, foreign trade and the population have sharply decreased, and the prosperity is no longer what it used to be. The city has a population of only about 100,000, and the number of Japanese and Koreans who have moved in is close to 70,000. The local area has already been reduced to a semi-colony. Everything looks to the Japanese, which is also heartbreaking.

Commemoration of Deceased Overseas Chinese Compatriots in Liaoning 64

The General Assembly Passed Five Resolutions to Telegraph the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for Negotiations

And Voted to Plan an Economic Embargo Against Japan

Shenyang Correspondence: On the afternoon of August 2nd, representatives from all sectors of Liaoning gathered at the Butterfly Grand Theater south of the Drum Tower in the city to hold a memorial service for the overseas Chinese compatriots who perished in Korea. More than 500 representatives from various agencies and groups attended. The meeting commenced at 11:30 a.m., presided over by Yan Yuheng. Mournful music was played, and formal respects were paid. The chairman presented a wreath and read a eulogy. Subsequently, the chairman reported the purpose of the meeting. Then, Liu Ziping, a representative of the afflicted overseas Chinese in Pyongyang, described the disasters and riots that had occurred. He stated that the tragedy of the overseas Chinese in Pyongyang was the worst of all regions. The property losses there were estimated to be over five million yuan. The number of deaths and injuries, based on what the Japanese could not conceal, each reached two hundred. Those whose fate was unknown or who sustained minor injuries also exceeded one hundred. Currently, about two thousand have fled back to Andong, and about four thousand two hundred have fled back to Yantai. More than a thousand remain in Pyongyang, scattered and destitute, awaiting death without any means of assistance. Taking our representatives as an example, we are originally from Shandong and have been doing business in Pyongyang for many years. Now, all the hard-earned gains of half a lifetime have been lost. We cannot maintain our livelihood in the future. The situation of overseas Chinese in Korea is similar, and it is unknown how many are in this predicament, etc. His words were extremely sorrowful, and the entire assembly was stirred up. Finally, the general assembly put forward five demands, requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to make serious representations to Japan via telegram. The entire assembly unanimously passed the following: (1) Punish the perpetrators and those responsible; (2) Compensate for all losses; (3) Apologize to our government; (4) Guarantee that such unfortunate events will not occur again in the future; (5) Our government should send troops to Korea to protect overseas Chinese. It was also resolved that the Foreign Affairs Association should plan an economic embargo against Japan. Subsequently, slogans were shouted, and the meeting adjourned. (August 2nd)

The Circumstances of the Murder of the 34th Division Commander 65

Regimental Commander Wang Junjie Was the Mastermind of the Murder

And Falsely Used the Name of the Entire Division to Usurp He's Position

The Headquarters Arrested Him for Strict Interrogation and Thorough Investigation

Hankou Correspondence: The original commander of the 34th Army Division was Yue Weijun. Later, because Yue was besieged during the suppression of the communists, the Wuhan Headquarters ordered He Zhenfan, the chief of staff of the division, to temporarily act as commander. Recently, news came that He had died in his defense area. The Headquarters then ordered Regimental Commander Wang Junjie to act as division commander. Now, it has been found that He Zhenfan was actually assassinated by Wang Junjie. The reason is that Wang Junjie was under He's command, and their opinions had always been inconsistent. Recently, in order to expand his own strength, he instructed soldiers in the Xiantao defense area to shoot and kill He Zhenfan, the acting division commander. Subsequently, he falsely used the names of the division officers to send a joint telegram requesting that Wang succeed as division commander. The wording was absurd and bordered on coercion. He Chengjun, the director of the Headquarters, had already learned of Wang's plot to seize military power and assassinate his superior. However, because Wang was leading troops in the defense area, he feared that acting too hastily would incite a rebellion. Therefore, he temporarily showed tolerance and allowed him to succeed in order to reassure him. A few days ago, Director He telegraphed Wang, saying that there were important matters to discuss in person, urging him to come to Hankou quickly. Wang believed it to be true and arrived on time. He then had Wang arrested and escorted to the Headquarters military law office yesterday. He also reported to the commander-in-chief and organized a military law trial for strict interrogation and thorough investigation in order to punish the lawless and enforce military discipline. As for the vacancies of the 34th Division commander and the regimental commander, Regimental Commander Zhang Wanxin has been appointed as acting division commander, and Jiang Hongmo has been promoted to acting regimental commander, respectively.

The Tragic Scene of the Yangtze River Flood 66

Jiujiang and Wuhu are Vast and Featureless; Trains, Airplanes, and Telegrams are All Suspended

Embankments Collapsed, Houses, Livestock, and Crops Were Swept Away

Northern Jiangxi Sent Urgent Reports of the Disaster; the Provincial Relief Conference Hastened Relief Efforts

Jiangxi Province Correspondence: For the past few days, there has been continuous rain and cold weather. As the saying goes, "Summer cold brings flooding," and indeed it has come to pass. According to those who have come from Jiujiang to the province, the Yangtze River flood has caused widespread disaster, and all the major commercial ports along the river have been submerged. The fields and villages on both banks are even worse. Since the 25th, low-lying areas in Jiujiang City, such as the roads along the river, South Gate Lake, Longchi Temple, and West Gate, have been flooded. Most of the shops have closed. Recently, as the water level continued to rise, all the roads were several feet deep, and traffic was cut off, requiring boats for transportation. Most residents have moved upstairs or relocated elsewhere. The daily necessities for those avoiding the flood must be purchased by small boats, and the boatmen are making several times their usual profit. The Yangtze River vessels cannot dock because their hawsers have been broken, and the pontoons are floating uncontrollably. Passengers must use small boats to get on and off the ships, but the wind is strong, and the waves are high, so the small boats often capsize, making it extremely dangerous. The Jiujiang airfield has also been several feet underwater recently, and planes from Shanghai and Chengdu cannot land, causing airmail to be suspended. The Shahe, Tujiapu, and Yongxiu areas of the Nanxun Railway are flooded by mountain torrents and river water, and much of the railway bridge and track have been submerged or washed away, so the railway has been closed since the 27th. Mail from Jiujiang to the province is piled up like mountains. It has been five days since a train from Shanghai has arrived in this city. Although mail from the Nanxun line is now being sent by small steamers, it takes at least two days to arrive. Many of the telegraph lines along the Yangtze River have been submerged or washed away, and all lines from the province to Shanghai and Hankou are completely cut off. Official telegrams are being sent by wireless, but because of the congestion of official telegrams, commercial telegrams have been temporarily suspended, causing extreme slowness in receiving news from this province. Merchants have no knowledge of market conditions in Shanghai and other ports. This is the situation regarding the difficulty of transportation in southern Jiangxi. As for the disaster situation, according to news from Jiujiang, the embankments in Jiujiang, Pengze, Hukou, Ruichang, Xingzi and other counties in northern Jiangxi along the river have been completely destroyed. Crops such as early rice and soybeans that were about to be harvested have been completely lost. Chickens, dogs, cattle, sheep and other livestock have been swept away. On the riverbanks and embankments, small houses have been swept away by the waves, and only the roofs of the tall houses are visible. According to a gentleman who came from Hankou to the province yesterday, from Hankou to Jiujiang, the water and sky blend into one color, with only a few treetops and sails visible. The carcasses of dead livestock and destroyed belongings float up and down with the waves, which is extremely tragic. In a village in Chi Kou, hundreds of thatched and brick houses are now nowhere to be seen. On Laozhoutou at the mouth of the Yangtze River in Hukou, there are more than one hundred houses and more than one thousand residents, but now only a few dozen roofs are visible, with the victims wailing on top. The water of Poyang Lake is discharged from the Yangtze River, but now the water of the Yangtze River is flowing back into the lake. In addition, mountain torrents from the Gan River and Rao River basins have overflowed the riverbanks, causing widespread flooding. The Poyang and Duchang areas have become a vast marsh, and the early rice crops have been completely destroyed. The situation is similar in the areas along the Yuan River and Gan River basins, but slightly less severe. As of today, the counties that have reported disasters include Pengze, Hukou, Yongxiu, Xinjian, Poyang, Dean, Shanggao, Fengcheng, Nanchang, Jiujiang, Ruichang, etc. The Provincial Relief Committee is currently preparing for emergency relief, and the Water Conservancy Bureau of the Department of Construction is also receiving funds from the Department of Finance and sending personnel to the embankments in northern Jiangxi for emergency repairs. (July 30th)

The Water Level Still Rises After Opening the Chelou Dam 67

Mao Yisheng Reports the Water Situation to the Provincial Government

The Provincial Government Approves Opening Two More Dams in Case of Emergency

This year's flood in Jiangsu Province has caused disaster, and the water level in the Grand Canal is rising daily. On the 2nd of this month, the Chelou Dam in Gaoyou was opened, but in less than a day, the watermark at Yumatou rose another inch (reaching one zhang, eight chi, and nine cun). Mao Yisheng, the Director of the Water Conservancy Bureau, returned to the province from Gaoyou yesterday (the 4th) and attended a meeting of the Provincial Government to report on the water situation. The Provincial Government immediately decided on the following measures for the counties to protect the embankments: (1) The entire eastern embankment of each county should be raised, temporarily set at three chi above the current water level, i.e., to resist water at two zhang and two cun (Yumatou watermark); the western embankment should be raised by referring to the eastern embankment and the situation west of the embankment; (2) All eastern and western embankments near cities, towns, and villages will be the responsibility of the county to which they belong, and all labor, materials, and expenses will be handled by the respective counties; (3) All eastern and western embankments outside the scope of the preceding provisions will be the responsibility of the Water Conservancy Bureau, but the respective counties should be responsible for recruiting laborers; (4) Each county along the river should recruit 1,500 laborers for the Water Conservancy Bureau, send personnel to lead them to work, and be subject to dispatch, with food provided by the Bureau; (5) The Water Conservancy Bureau will send personnel to each county to work with the county magistrate to demarcate responsible areas. Item 6 of the matters discussed by the Provincial Government that day stated that Director Mao and others telegraphed from Gaoyou on the 3rd, stating that the water still rose to 1.89 after opening the Chelou Dam yesterday, and that opening the Nanxin and Liang Dams would be necessary to avert danger, requesting instructions on the matter. It was resolved that the Nanxin and Liang Dams would be approved to be opened if the water level continued to rise unabated and was deemed to be dangerous. That day, Mao Yisheng left the province to inspect the water situation along the canal. It is reported that the Huai River in Bengbu has slightly receded in recent days. (August 5th)

Local Correspondence

Songjiang 68

Standing Committee Meeting of the Food Management Committee: Our county's Food Management Committee, after the County Government appointed Zhou and others as members, was organized according to regulations with the County Magistrate as the chairman. The first Standing Committee meeting was held yesterday, chaired by County Magistrate Shen. It was resolved that the expenses of the committee would be determined by the general affairs section drafting an expenditure budget, to be discussed and decided at the next meeting.

Preparing to Organize a Relief Home: The County Government held a county administration meeting today (the 5th), chaired by County Magistrate Shen. It was proposed that the Pest Control Committee is now planning to convene regularly, and it should be discussed how its expenses should be raised. Previously, with the approval of all sectors of the four counties, its term was extended for two months. All unfinished matters will be transferred to the Songjiang-Shanghai Regional Pacification Command for handling.

Suzhou 69

The Sodomy Case of a Lawyer Sent Back for Retrial: Shanghai lawyer Ren Zhennan was accused by his wife, Jiang Xingjuan, of sodomy and assault. The Shanghai District Prosecutor's Office ruled to dismiss the case. Jiang Xingjuan refused to accept the decision and filed a petition with the High Court to request a review. The High Prosecutor's Office attached great importance to this case and has already ruled to send it back to the Shanghai District Court for further investigation.

The Appeal Hearing of the Nun's Theft Case: Qing Shan, a nun from the Lujia Guanyin Hall on Changbang Road, Shanghai, colluded with Zhang Youren to illegally sell 2.6 mu of temple property and cemetery land in Xujiawan to others. They exhumed and relocated seven coffins to the International Cemetery, earning a total of 5,200 yuan. After the elderly nun Jin Lin discovered this, she sued in the Shanghai District Court, which sentenced Qing Shan to three years in prison and acquitted Zhang Youren. Qing Shan refused to accept the decision and appealed to the High Court. Yesterday (the 5th), a hearing was held, but because additional evidence was needed, the hearing was postponed.

Telegram Requesting the Rejection of Wu Lien-teh: The Suzhou Anti-Drug Association telegraphed the National Government's Anti-Smoking Committee, stating: "Previously, your committee complied with public opinion and abolished the Anti-Smoking Investigation Office, the news of which gladdened the entire country. However, newspapers are reporting that a National Narcotics Management Office will be established, and Mr. Wu Lien-teh has just returned from overseas. Commentators suspect that this is a disguised form of the Investigation Office, and Wu will be appointed as its director to reward his advocacy of public sale. We know that your committee is thoroughly banning smoking and will not make the same mistake twice. However, unfounded rumors may become reality. Therefore, we urgently request you to issue a statement to dispel rumors and reject Mr. Wu to distance ourselves from villainous individuals and maintain credibility."

Wuxi 70

The Finance Bureau Seeks Bids for Contracting the Feast Donation: Wang Jingzhi, the Director of the County Finance Bureau, stated that the county's feast education donation had previously been contracted to Xu Shide, a merchant, until the end of June of this year. After the contract was terminated, former Director Shen notified all restaurants to continue collecting donations as before and await assignment for collection. At the same time, a notice was issued inviting merchants to bid. However, after two deadlines, no one bid, and the donation collection was suspended, leaving education expenses without funding. This was brought up at a county administration meeting, and it was resolved that for July of this year, the Finance Bureau would audit the accounts of each restaurant to verify and collect the donations, and at the same time, quickly invite merchants to bid for contracting the donation. It should be noted that the original target amount was 24,000 yuan per year, but it has now been reduced to 18,000 yuan. The public bidding is scheduled for 10:00 a.m. on the 15th of this month.

Suspected of Theft, Resentment Leads to Self-Harm: A resident in the No. 53 workshop of the Jinji Silk Factory outside the West Gate of our county, a detective Wu from the Water Police District, had a white Xiangyun silk gown stolen by a thief a few days ago. He conducted a thorough investigation, but there were no clues. Unexpectedly, Jiang Asi, who lived with him, thought that even though he had not committed the theft, he could not avoid suspicion due to their cohabitation. He felt extremely resentful. At 6:00 p.m. the day before yesterday, Asi left alone and went to a tavern to drink heavily. After returning home, he took a kitchen knife and slashed his head several times, causing blood to flow immediately, and he fell to the ground unconscious. His elder brother, Bingkui, found him and immediately hired a car to take him to the Puren Hospital for treatment. However, his injuries were severe, and his life was in danger.

Bandits Robbed Repeatedly; One Was Captured: On the night of the 4th, at around 10:00 p.m., more than ten bandits suddenly arrived at the home of Zhang Fuguan, a villager in Xuehuaijiang Village near Zhangcun Town in the fifth district of our county (Tianshang City). Each of them carried fake handguns and appeared fierce, intending to rob. At that time, Zhang's family, both men and women, were cooling off in the open space. When they saw the bandits arrive, they dared not speak. The bandits then rushed into the house and robbed them extensively, taking more than ten yuan in silver. They then went to the northern street of Shitou Town to rob a net-carrying boat parked on the riverbank. As a result, the boat owner's wife's gold earrings were also robbed, with a total loss of about twenty yuan. Dissatisfied, the bandits went to Xie Renguan's home in Shenxiang Village in Xintangli and aimed a fake handgun at Xie Renguan, pretending to fire. When Renguan saw this, he knew it was a fake gun and immediately gathered his neighbors to bravely capture the bandit. One bandit was captured on the spot. Later, the captured bandit was identified as a local villager.

Bandits Sent Letters Demanding Huge Sums of Money: Wang Shaoxian, a resident of Cotton Lane outside the South Gate of our county, is a wealthy merchant from Anhui living in Wuxi, and a shareholder of the Gansheng Silk Factory under the Gongyun Bridge. He is now over sixty years old and quite famous for his wealth. Recently, he suddenly received a threatening letter from Shanghai, which stated that he should lend 20,000 silver dollars, otherwise, unfavorable measures would be taken against him. After Wang received the letter, he burned it. This was discovered by Wang Weixin, the director of the third branch of the Public Security Bureau, who immediately sent a police officer to investigate and secretly deployed police to prevent accidents.

A Vast Area Reported Crop Failure Due to the Flood: Since the beginning of summer, our county has been experiencing continuous rain and rising river water. Low-lying fields in the countryside have turned into marshes, and farmers are displaced, which is unbearable to see. Moreover, the green seedlings have rotted, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. The disastrous situation is rare in recent years. Zhu Chenghong, the head of the fifth district, and Yu Shangshu, the head of the eleventh district, have recently received reports of crop failure from the town chiefs and farmers in their respective districts. In Tianshang City, 2,000 mu of fields marked "Qiu," 800 mu marked "Lie," and 500 mu marked "Xue" have been affected. In the Ganlu Town area of Nanyan City, more than ten thousand mu have been affected. Yesterday, the district reported the situation to the County Government, requesting that personnel be sent to the countryside to investigate the disaster and seek relief.

Ammunition Truck Explodes in Lingkou: Luo Laiqiu, Battalion Commander of the Third Battalion of the Independent Artillery Regiment of the National Army Fourth Division stationed in Hangzhou, sent a battalion adjutant with soldiers to the capital on the 2nd to collect artillery shells, etc. They then loaded a freight car numbered 8008, attached to the rear of freight car number 206. On the morning of the 3rd, around 5 a.m., the car arrived at Lingkou Station and stopped. While detaching the car, an unexpected violent collision occurred, causing the ammunition to explode, injuring seven people including Battalion Adjutant Wang Renjie, soldiers Dai Liwen, Chen Rengui, and Liu Liande. Arriving at Changzhou Station, four people including Wang Jie were injured and sent to Wujin Hospital for treatment. Three lightly injured people continued to Hangzhou with the car.

Zhenjiang 72

Surveying Flood Damage in One District: Last month, there was continuous rain for ten days. Various districts in this county reported famine. The county government sent personnel to survey the area. Surveying committee members Li Shaoan and Huo Rentai, together with District Chief Zhang Zuwu of that district, went to Taoyuan, Helin, and Jihua townships under their jurisdiction three days ago to conduct surveys, which have been completed. The survey showed that in those townships where the terrain is higher, the beans in the mountain fields were destroyed by the water. In the lower fields, the seedlings were submerged by the water, but efforts can still be made to provide relief. The disaster in Jiaodong and Yonggu townships is very serious. The water depth is nearly one zhang (approximately 10 feet) in the deep areas, and more than two chi (approximately 2 feet) in the shallow areas. The farmers are in dire need of disaster relief. Areas such as Dingyezhou and Buyezhou mainly rely on reeds for income. In the above townships, a total of 24,000 mu of fields were affected by the disaster, and approximately 40 places were affected by broken dikes and destroyed houses, with approximately 12,000 disaster victims.

Danyang County Magistrate Wang Again Accused: Danyang County Magistrate Wang Jiwu is accused of accepting bribes while serving as Jingjiang County Magistrate in handling a opium case. The case was filed with the High Court, which designated the Zhenjiang Court as having jurisdiction. A court hearing had already been held once for investigation. Now, Chen Yaoqun of Jingjiang also accuses Wang of embezzling fines from opium cases during his tenure. The case has also been accepted and the court is now investigating the files of the opium case in Jingjiang County and summoning Wang for questioning.

Condition of Cotton Crops in Tongtai: The cotton crop in the Tong area this year, along the Yunyan River and in the salt field areas, has suffered extremely heavy losses due to floods, and the autumn harvest is hopeless. Hangzhou 75

Provincial Government Executes Bandit Leader for Kidnapping: The Zhejiang Provincial Government, in the case of the kidnapping of Wu Jiaxiang, a wealthy merchant from Cixi, and his son, and the extortion of 28,400 yuan, ordered the execution of bandit leader Cheng Guoliang, also known as Wang Agen, who had a knife scar about an inch long on his face. He was recognized by Wu Shenshi, the wife of the victim Wu Jiaxiang, who encountered him at a small vegetable market in Hongkou, Shanghai, and tracked him to his residence. Later, Yao County captured Zhang Guoming, an accomplice in the case, who had already been approved for execution. He also confessed the name and address of Cheng Guoliang, which matched the information obtained by Wu Shenshi. The provincial government sent detectives to Shanghai to arrest and bring him to justice. However, the criminal cunningly refused to confess. The victim was summoned to court for questioning, and it was proven that the criminal was present and involved in the kidnapping from the beginning to the repeated negotiations and payment of money. The evidence was solid, and he was sentenced to death in accordance with the regulations for punishing kidnappers. Yesterday (the 5th) at 8 a.m., officials were sent to bring the bandit leader forward, verify his identity, and escort him to the Qingbomen execution ground for execution by firing squad.

Letter Requesting the Allocation of Funds to Clean Up Public Debt: The Zhejiang Provincial Government sent a letter to the Liangzhe Salt Transport Envoy Office yesterday, stating: "Respectfully, after investigation, the province issued 8 million yuan in public bonds to clean up old debts. All regulations have been promulgated by the National Government. This public bond is specifically used to clean up old debts and should be raised through various means in order to repay the old debts separately. In 1929, the province issued construction public bonds and sent a letter to your office requesting that salt merchants be persuaded to subscribe on behalf of the province, but this was not approved. Now, we reiterate the previous proposal and change the subscription to 500,000 yuan in public bonds to clean up old debts. We hope that you will immediately convene various salt merchants to allocate subscriptions separately and order them to pay the funds as soon as possible for prompt transfer."

Ningbo 76

Ordered to Abolish the Municipal Committee: After the abolition of the Ningbo Municipal Government, all municipal affairs are handled by the Yin County Government. However, citizens believe that the scope of municipal affairs being merged into the Yin County Government is too large, and they advocate for the establishment of a Yin County Municipal Committee to assist the government. The regulations and election methods of the committee have been approved and promulgated by the provincial government. Furthermore, the Yin County Government has been ordered to select ten members of the Municipal Committee from among the village chiefs of the Village and Village Committees and report them to the provincial government for approval. Now it is learned that after receiving the administrative report from the Zhejiang Provincial Government, the Ministry of Interior believes that the organization of the committee not only has no legal basis but also retains a municipal agency after the abolition of the Municipal Government, which may hinder the administrative system. Therefore, the ministry immediately sent a letter to the Zhejiang Provincial Government, urging it to change the merger in order to comply with the regulations. After receiving the letter, the provincial government decided at the provincial affairs meeting to order the Yin County Government to inform the Municipal Committee to abolish the report. The Yin County Government has received this order yesterday and will report the abolition of the Municipal Committee.

Major Fire in Daqitou: A fire broke out at the Wang family's Tianbao Hall in Daqitou, Yan Township, Zhenhai. An elderly woman, planning to go to incense at Zhaobao Mountain, got up to cook rice around 3 a.m. yesterday. She forgot about the fire, which ignited a pile of grass. The woman did not notice it until around 4 a.m., when a blaze suddenly erupted. It took three hours to extinguish the fire. It is estimated that more than 100 street houses were burned down, from Baoshan cigarette paper shop in the east to Dexing mounting shop, and from Wang Ruichang rice shop in the west to the residential houses. The loss is estimated at more than 100,000 yuan.

Wang Renqi Kidnapped: Wang Renqi, from Maoxing, Fenghua, is quite wealthy. Yesterday, four or five bandits suddenly arrived and kidnapped Wang, demanding a large ransom. His family is afraid of being kidnapped again and plans to move to the city temporarily to avoid the danger.

Preparations for the Annual Meeting of the Science Society are Ready 78

To be held in Zhenjiang on August 22nd

The 16th Annual Meeting of the China Science Society is scheduled to be held in Zhenjiang from August 22nd to 26th this year. The various preparatory committees for the annual meeting have been working separately for some time and held a preparatory conference in Zhenjiang last month. Now, the preparations are gradually coming to an end. A handbook for the annual meeting has been sent to each member. The preparation situation is recorded as follows: (1) The accommodation for members is designated at Jiaoshan, which can accommodate 150 people for meals and accommodation, and the daily round-trip ferry will be provided by the Jiangsu Provincial Government. (2) The Ministry of Railways has approved a 50% discount on train tickets for members traveling to and from the meeting on all railways nationwide. (3) The conference and public lectures will be held in the auditorium of the Jiangsu Department of Education and Zhenjiang Park. The Society Affairs Committee and paper presentations will be held in the Yijiang Building in Jiaoshan. Presenting papers is the most important part of the Society's annual meeting. To date, more than 30 papers have been received, each with a summary, which has been compiled and printed by the Paper Committee for distribution to each member at the annual meeting to facilitate joint discussion. In addition to the papers, experts from the society will report on the progress of various sciences over the past year. (4) A small-scale exhibition of domestic scientific achievements is planned to be held during the annual meeting. Exhibits from Guangzhou, Beiping, Nanjing, and other places have already been sent. This is the first time the society has tried to do this. (5) Public banquets will be hosted by the Jiangsu Provincial Government, the Zhenjiang General Chamber of Commerce, the Departments of Agriculture and Mining, Construction, and Education, and the China United Sericulture Improvement Association. In addition, there will be tea parties hosted by the Zhenjiang Society Friends Association, the Nanyang, Tangshan, and Hehai University Alumni Associations. (6) On the fifth day of the annual meeting, the entire group will visit Yangzhou, hosted by Yangzhou Middle School. A public lecture will be held in the school's newly built auditorium, which can accommodate 1,500 people. (7) The officers of the annual meeting committees are as follows: (1) Annual Meeting General Committee: Wu Jingheng, Chairman; Yang Xiaoshu, Secretary; Deng Fupei, Accountant; Mao Yisheng, Propaganda; Sun Hongzhe, Chen Hexian, Liu Yizheng, Yu Qingtang, Zhou Houxu. (2) Paper Committee: Weng Wenhao, Chairman; Bing Zhi, Wang Jin, He Yanxuan, He Yujie, Zhu Kezhen, Bao Guobao, Hui Cheng. (3) Arrangement Committee: Zhou Ren, Chairman; Hu Gangfu, Ren Hongjun, Qian Baozong, Lu Minxing. (4) Lecture Committee: Wang Jin, Chairman; Yang Quan, Wang Maozu, Zhu Wenxin, Mao Yisheng. (5) Reception Committee: Lu Feizhi, Chairman; Deng Fu, Fang Yipu, Chen Liren, Pei Yixiang, Ge Jingzhong, Zhou Houxu. (6) Social Committee: Yu Qingtang, Chairman; Ye Jiajun, Lu Xiaohou, Guan Jian, Deng Fupei.

Zhejiang Provincial Medical School Renamed to Vocational School 79

Ordered by the Ministry to Continue Operations and Start Enrolling New Students

The Zhejiang Provincial Medical and Pharmaceutical School has been quite successful since its establishment. Four years ago, due to changes in the academic system, the Ministry of Education considered medicine and pharmacy to be advanced education, and a four-year graduation was deemed insufficient. An order was issued to stop enrollment and gradually end the school. Currently, only one class of fourth-year medical and pharmaceutical students remains, and they will graduate by the end of this year. Recently, due to the appeals of the medical and pharmaceutical community in Hangzhou, the Ministry of Education has approved the continuation of operations, but the school should be renamed the Medical and Pharmaceutical Vocational School. Yesterday, the school received an order from the Department of Education and immediately convened a school affairs meeting to appoint eleven teachers to form an enrollment committee. The enrollment period is set for the 15th of this month. This time, 60 medical students and 40 pharmacy students will be recruited. Those who have graduated from high school are qualified to apply.

Hangzhou West Street, the second part of the Zhejiang Provincial First Middle School, was renamed the Zhejiang Provincial Girls' Middle School this year, and Sun Jianwen was appointed as the principal. This was reported in this newspaper. The school is currently repairing school buildings and preparing for the start of the semester. It is heard that there are many applicants for the junior high school this time. It is now learned that the Department of Education decided yesterday to add a high school department to the school, recruiting 40 new students for the first grade of the general high school course. The school will start preparing for enrollment as soon as the order arrives.

Minutes of the Veterinary Education Promotion Association Meeting 84

The China Veterinary Education Promotion Association held its second meeting the day before yesterday. Cai Wuji, Wang Zhaoji, Ye Hancheng, Shen Jiucheng, Yang Weiyu, Pan Yangyao and others attended the meeting and resolved the following matters: (1) Revised and approved the association's rules. (2) The association's location is temporarily set up at the China Vocational Education Society. (3) Mr. Yang Weiyu was recommended to handle the association's filing procedures. (4) Add charitable words to the purpose of the veterinary vocational school to arouse the attention of philanthropists. (5) In addition to the 40 student places in the medical vocational school, add 10 elective student places. (Both male and female students are admitted, focusing on animal husbandry) (6) Recommend Zou Bingwen, Cai Wuji, Wang Zhaoji, Ye Hancheng, Shen Jiucheng, Yang Weiyu, and Pan Yangyao as standing committee members of the association. The purpose book for establishing the veterinary vocational school, which was published yesterday, is explored as follows: The basis of human life is nothing more than three kinds of moving plants and minerals, especially animals are the largest. All the needs of food, clothing, housing and transportation are related to livestock and poultry. There are meat, milk, eggs, wool, feathers, and service. We take their strengths as a resource to use for our life. The contribution of beasts and birds to human life should be very great. Since science is prosperous and academic evolution, human beings already have eugenics, and beasts and birds also have selective breeding methods. Pure breeds require strength, and their reproduction and growth are required, and inferior breeds must be eliminated. With the power of artificial, to make up for the lack of natural, not only to help the economy, but also to benefit the people. It is the duty of a veterinarian to examine and inspect the diseases and ailments of beasts and birds and to treat them, just as humans have diseases and seek treatment from doctors, and beasts and birds are also living animals. Recently, in Europe, the United States and other countries, medicine is prosperous, and it has progressed from treating people to treating beasts and birds. There are schools for training, and there are specialized talents. They have close relationships in hygiene administration, agricultural technology, commodity inspection, and type improvement. Excellent breeds can be used to produce a large number of fruits, which can prevent the spread of inferior breeds and prevent diseases and pests of beasts and birds. The strengths of the beasts and birds are used to give them their effect. Veterinarians are really meeting the requirements of the times and occupying an important position today. Recently, science is prevalent in my country, and new policies have been introduced one after another. Since the selection of species, animal husbandry, aquaculture, slaughter, disease, commodity inspection, manufacturing and other important tasks, specialized talents are needed to manage them, and the most lacking are veterinarians. Shanghai is a major port in southeastern China, and it occupies an important position in the world. Recently, various businesses have been organized in order, but no attention has been paid to the facilities of veterinary education, which is a disease for those who know it. Everyone has a heart of empathy. Since there is medical treatment for human poverty and illness, the diseases of beasts and birds should also be treated equally. Therefore, in the spirit of the Western Inscription, the people of my country are compatriots and the world is involved. The establishment of veterinary medicine is also a kind of charity. Therefore, veterinary experts, administrative authorities, and education comrades are gathered together to form a committee to promote veterinary education. We will earnestly study the plan for training veterinary talents to meet the technical needs of agricultural administrative agencies, health administrative agencies, agricultural education agencies, and commodity inspection agencies in various provinces and cities. First, we will entrust the China Vocational Education Society to run the veterinary vocational school. The curriculum should not be too deep, but be practical. The level should not be too high, but be appropriate. Take theory as the foundation and practice as the application. The meaning is nothing more than to arouse the concept of the Chinese people's attention to veterinary medicine, and to train professional talents, to increase efficiency for the cause, and to make a small contribution to society. If the wise and honorable officials and enthusiastic comrades in the country can give assistance, it is even more hoped.

Hunan University Hires Professors in Shanghai 85

The school's prospectus lists several items for parents and students to note: (1) exclusively admitting male students and exclusively admitting boarding students; (2) stricter management and more teaching hours; (3) students may attend a one-month trial period; if dissatisfied with the school's educational methods, they may request withdrawal at any time, and fees will be refunded in full.
