Free Talk

A Word of Advice 112

— Yi Mei

Those who frequently date their lovers are bound to have more accurate watches.

Judging a person's appetite by their build is often inaccurate.

The greatest joys in life lie within family relationships, not in indulging in feasts and entertainment.

Good things are not cheap, and cheap things are not good. Therefore, advertisements promising "cheap and good" only reveal the merchant's deceit.

The more one labors during the day, the sweeter one's sleep at night.

Emotional wounds are difficult to heal.

Sharp and sarcastic writing can diminish one's blessings. We writers should take this as a warning.

Those who become inspired after drinking are considered talented; those who complain are just being sour.

The same livelihood problem can lead some to live frugally and maintain integrity, while others resort to deceit and exploitation. This distinguishes the virtuous from the petty.

Young men and women are easily united but also easily separated. Therefore, the Matchmaker's marriage registry has become a confusing mess beyond comprehension.

Tall buildings do not necessarily house great people.

Dragonflies swarm before a summer rain. Thus, dragonflies are the heralds of rain.

Sweet girls and passionate ladies are the only idols worthy of worship in the eyes of modern people.

One should watch Bardsley's movies in the summer and Clara Bow's movies in the winter. One is cold, and one is hot, subtly balancing each other.

Spiderwebs in the corner of a room, illuminated by the cool moonlight, evoke a sense of desolation.

Those who are enthusiastic cannot be cooled down, even by drinking ice and swallowing snow.

A Brief Record of the Liangjiang Scouts Camping 113

— Xu Shoujian

The Shanghai Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School, famous for its basketball team, has been established for many years and is well-known far and wide. This year's graduates, feeling their studies were insufficient, established a summer program at the Wusong Fisheries School. On the first of the month, the scouts from the program camped at the public sports field outside the South Gate of Baoshan. The following is a jumbled account of the events.

Barefoot Immortals Running Through the Streets: Baoshan is located in a remote coastal area. Although close to Shanghai, its customs and traditions are still considered closed off. One afternoon, in the poor countryside of Baoshan, groups of women with bare legs were suddenly discovered, playing and frolicking. For a time, onlookers were amazed and exclaimed, "Where did these shameless Barefoot Immortals come from?"

Brisk Business for Watermelons and Soda: Recently, the weather has been extremely hot, with the scorching sun in the sky. As soon as the female scouts' tents were pitched, they felt covered in sweat and complained of the heat. As a result, the business of general soda and snack vendors boomed. A certain tea server at the sports field, originally a nearby farmer, carried several loads of watermelons to sell. Before long, they were all sold out, and his pockets were bulging, causing him to grin from ear to ear.

Gentle Breeze Opens a Field Meeting: At 8 PM, a camping field meeting was held. The residents of Baoshan City, young and old, came out in droves to watch. At the sound of a police whistle, the entire group lined up in a circle. Straw was burned in the center. In the flickering firelight, Coach Leng Xueqiao gave a brief report, saying, "Our school is honored to gather with the people of your area. However, due to insufficient prior preparation, the program performed at today's field meeting will be very simple and will fail to meet the high expectations of the guests. We hope you will forgive us. All those attending today are graduates of this year's Liangjiang School. As separation is imminent, we deeply hope that all students will display their best skills to embellish this rare event." Ms. Liu was then elected as chairwoman. Everyone held hands and walked around the circle, dancing and singing a song called "The Chinese Boy Scout Song." The singing was loud and clear, piercing through the clouds, expressing a spirit of excitement and enthusiasm. Next was the performance of various recreational activities, including several types of fan dances and excellent dances. The dancing was graceful and elegant, earning a lot of applause. A certain lady's Charleston dance, with its thick waist, wiggling and swaying feet, was quite amusing. Finally, everyone sang the Liangjiang School song together and dispersed, having enjoyed themselves to the fullest. By then, it was already ten o'clock.

Small Recipes 114

— Yang Yi Xiao

Braised Taro with Pork Belly: Cut the taro in half. Cut the pork belly into square pieces. Add soy sauce and rock sugar to the pot and braise over high heat. Remove and taste when cooked. It is exceptionally rich and delicious.

Stir-fried Green Beans with Shrimp: Fry the green beans and shelled fresh shrimp in a hot wok with lard. Add a little soy sauce and stir two or three times. It is tender and delicious.

Winter Melon Stuffed with Ham: Peel and seed the winter melon, cut it into square pieces, and stuff it with shredded ham. Soak it in boiling water, and add a little chicken broth and salt. It tastes exceptionally delicious.

Lo Su with Chicken Slices: Peel and split the lo su (a type of melon). Slice the chicken thinly and stuff it inside. Cook it in a wok with soy sauce. It is exceptionally delicious and savory.

Interesting Aerial Events 115

— Qiu Shui

In recent years, tragic accidents involving airplanes have often been reported in the newspapers. Although the world's science is progressing day by day, air travel is still not entirely safe, at least for the time being.

The dangers faced by airplanes in the sky are mostly due to sudden changes in weather or damage to the aircraft. However, in addition to these, according to historical aviation records, there are some unexpected dangers. These seem so interesting that I have named this article "Interesting Aerial Events."

For example, in early April of this year, a long-distance flight from Marseille, France, to Paris carried several passengers and some luggage. Among the luggage were several boxes of bees brought by someone. In the middle of the flight, for some reason, a swarm of bees from one of the boxes suddenly broke free and flew around the passengers and pilots, engaging in their aggressive activities. Imagine a small airplane with limited space. Now, with so many annoying little clowns, it was impossible to defend against them and impossible to avoid them. Wouldn't they be crying in agony? The pilot was especially miserable. He had to pay attention to the machinery and the safety of the passengers. How could his two hands move freely? He had no choice but to let the bees sting him freely. He was only freed from his suffering when he reached his destination, but his whole body was covered in wounds.

On another occasion, during the European war, a British plane crossed the English Channel to fly to Europe. There was only one passenger on board. In the middle of the flight, he suddenly went crazy, pulled out a pistol, aimed it at the pilot, and demanded that he jump out of the plane together. The pilot looked down and saw that the plane was still flying over the vast ocean. He frowned and came up with a plan. He politely said to the passenger, "Sir, please go down first. I will follow you." The madman fell for it, and the pilot saved his life.

On another occasion, a commercial airplane was flying when it was discovered that an important part of the machine had malfunctioned. For the safety of the passengers, the pilot landed the plane and carefully inspected it. He found that several rats were nesting near the part. He immediately chased them away and repaired the part before resuming the flight.

In another instance, in a certain part of Africa, an explorer took a plane and flew low over the plains to inspect the area. Suddenly, a lion pounced on the plane and damaged its wing. Also, Prince George of England recently traveled in India, using an airplane for transportation. Eagles often swooped down from the sky and damaged the plane's machinery. In a certain part of the United States, a pilot fell to his death after eagles attacked his plane. How can such unexpected dangers be fully prevented?

Emperor Hui of Ming and the Great Zha Mountain in Hang County 116

— Xiao Chang

With relics of Minister Cheng Ji's peach and the Emperor's Stone

During the Jingnan Campaign at the beginning of the Ming Dynasty, unofficial histories recorded that Emperor Jianwen was tonsured as a monk and escaped through a tunnel, with his whereabouts unknown. The world regarded the emperor as having abdicated the throne, while the official history of the Ming Dynasty strongly refuted this, claiming that Jianwen and his palace had committed self-immolation and died for the country. However, according to local elders, Jianwen once resided at Dongming Temple on the Great Zha Mountain in the northern countryside of Hang County. Relics still remain and are clearly verifiable. This makes the accounts in the unofficial histories credible. The following is a record of Jianwen's residence at Great Zha Mountain and related relics, provided for researchers of Ming history to examine.

Great Zha Mountain is located at the intersection of Hang County, Deqing, and Wukang, fifty li outside the Hulin Gate of Hangzhou. It rises high above the clouds, with a circumference of over thirty li. Climbing to its peak, one can look south towards the Zhe River, where the water appears as a ribbon and the masts and sails are faintly visible. Looking north, one can see Wukang, with the houses on Mount Mogan clearly countable. From this, one can imagine the mountain's height. The mountain is covered in lush bamboo and trees, and the scenery is serene. On the peak of the mountain, there is a Taoist temple called Qingzhen Temple, inhabited by Taoist priests. Three li away from the temple, on the mountainside, there is a Buddhist temple called Dongming Temple, a place for monks to practice Zen. Both the temple and the Taoist temple were built during the Zhiyuan period of the Yuan Dynasty.

During the Jingnan Campaign at the beginning of the Ming Dynasty, it is said that Emperor Jianwen shaved his head and became a monk. The court official Cheng Ji dressed as a Taoist and fled with him, exiting through a tunnel in the palace and secretly heading towards Dusongguan in western Zhejiang (located seventy-five li northwest of Yu Hang County, a strategic pass in Jiangsu and Zhejiang). From Dusongguan, they went to the Great Zha Mountain in the northern countryside of Hang County and hid there. However, the two lived separately, with Jianwen residing at Dongming Temple and Cheng Ji practicing alchemy at Qingzhen Temple. From then on, the two rulers led an otherworldly life. Qingzhen Temple and Dongming Temple are directly above each other, and they could faintly see each other. After Jianwen and Cheng Ji hid there, every dawn, the two would come out of the mountain gate and look at each other from afar. Between the temple and the Taoist temple, there is a large, square rock, smooth and lustrous. On every new moon and full moon, the two would meet on the rock. This rock still exists today and is called the Emperor's Stone. Today, the mountain also has what is called Cheng Ji's Peach. The fruit is not very large and ripens in summer. When ripe, the pit and flesh separate, and the flesh near the pit is crimson. The taste is quite delicious and is a unique product of the mountain. It is said that this peach tree was planted by Cheng Ji, and its species has been passed down to this day, hence the name Cheng Ji's Peach.

In the side hall of Qingzhen Temple, there is an idol of Cheng Ji, dressed as a Taoist. In another room in the back hall of Dongming Temple, there is a statue of a monk, about thirty years old, wearing a robe, holding Buddhist beads, with lowered eyebrows and sitting in meditation. It is said that this statue is of Emperor Jianwen, who held the lofty position of power in the Ming Dynasty. Great Zha Mountain is only twelve li away from our town. The Qingzhen Temple holds its deity birthday celebration on the thirteenth day of the eighth month of each year, which is quite lively. I have visited twice and witnessed the above-mentioned relics.

News from the Art World: Gu Yue, whose alias is Gao Tianqi, is skilled in poetry and songwriting, and excels in fiction. His calligraphy is rooted in the Northern Wei style, with a charming posture within its strength. He intends to give away a hundred fan paintings to make connections with others. Those who wish to obtain Gao's calligraphy can send one yuan (stamps can be used as payment, with half-cent stamps as the limit) to Tianyi Film Company, Gan Shidong Road, French Concession, Shanghai. The work will be returned within five days.

Travels in India (75)

— Ling Hua

On the sixth, I attended the student arts and crafts fair at the Indian University with Dr. S.R.D. Sokda and his wife. The fair was in the auditorium, with over a thousand people in attendance, both male and female students. The electric fans were turned on. When guests arrived, ushers offered them a fresh flower and a sprig of pine on a tray. Soon after, they sprayed perfume on the seated guests with a perfume atomizer. This was an improvement over the colored water that people splashed on each other during the day. The perfume atomizer only sprayed a few drops on the head, whereas the colored water was splashed all over the body as a prank. After a while, the arts and crafts fair began. Boys and girls played music and sang. A strongman lifted iron rings weighing 115 pounds and rolled iron sheets with his hands as if rolling a rope. After rolling, he showed it to the seated guests. I saw that the iron sheet was about four-tenths of an inch thick and over an inch wide. No one could unbend the iron sheet that he had rolled. He could be said to be very brave. But his body was not very large or unusual. It was all due to practice. I left early because of the distance. Dr. Sokda and his wife went to their home. The moon was rising, and the shadows of the trees were swaying, so we had a night talk. Dr. Sokda and his wife are famous doctors who have been in England for a long time. They have a garden, so we discussed social medicine and hygiene. Most Indian priests are vegetarians and do not eat meat, as they consider meat to be unclean. According to them, they wished to use medical and hygiene laws to build a new village. The distribution of fields, houses, gardens, and all aspects of life, work, and even birth, upbringing, illness, old age, death, and burial, should all be governed by hygiene regulations. Property, equipment, livestock, and real estate that can be publicly owned should be publicly owned. Those that can be privately owned should be privately owned. All the households in the village, regardless of how many, should be guided and managed by doctors. They said that before a person is born, the mother's rights are important. After they are born, the doctor's rights should be important. The disposal of property, customs, and other matters should be based on hygiene. For example, the capitalist's slaves and workers go against hygiene rules. I asked, "If there is war and killing fills the fields, wouldn't that be even more against hygiene? What should be done?" They replied, "Medical professionals should unite the world's doctors with medical authority to abolish war, equally emphasizing maternal rights. Mothers give birth, and doctors protect. Then the world can be at peace." I said, "This reasoning is very good. In ancient China, the founders of the country were two doctors, Shennong and Huangdi. The founders of the Republic of China are also doctors, Sun Yat-sen. Only doctors know the importance of hygiene and protecting the people. Therefore, Chinese doctors should be both rulers and teachers. The plans of the ruler must include doctors. In a small scale, they can serve as the head of the new village. On a large scale, they can serve as the head of a country. This is the medical transformation of the great union. I hope that the world's doctors will unite and campaign for this." His wife, Ms. Gumlili, is very enthusiastic about social movements.

Novel Club

Woman, Woman (11) 117

— Yao Su Feng

Miss Ding instructed Qiu Zi, "I need to go out for a while. Let the old lady eat her supper and go to sleep first. Don't wait up for me." Qiu Zi agreed obediently.

Qiu Zi opened the door for them, and Mr. Lu and Miss Ding went out together. One walked in front, and the other followed behind. After they walked out of the gate, Qiu Zi saw that the one walking in front had stopped, and the one walking behind had caught up. Then they walked side by side.

"Where are you going?" Mr. Lu asked.

"I'd really like to play a little golf. Isn't the Dahua Golf Course nearby? Let's go to Dahua!" Miss Ding said.

Mr. Lu was a novice at golf. Miss Ding had played a few times, but she wasn't very skilled either. So they played very slowly, and their scores were very high. When they reached the eighth hole, Miss Ding looked down from a high place and suddenly saw someone standing there, it was Mr. Li who had come to her house earlier, looking up at her.

She was a little embarrassed. Although she didn't want to see him, she felt that she had to greet him when she saw him, especially since he had come to her house earlier.

While she was hesitating, Mr. Li walked up.

"Miss Ding! What are you doing here? I came to your house earlier, but your maid said you had already gone out. I never expected to meet you here!" Mr. Li turned around, deliberately acting as if he had just seen Mr. Lu, and then continued, "Ah! Little Lu! Great! You came with her?"

Mr. Lu was disgusted by the sight of him. He replied with an arrogant expression, "I specially invited Miss Ding to come together."

Metals: No New Developments in the Entire City 138

Market Overview: Yesterday's metal market conditions showed no significant progress from any of the trading guilds. As a result, the overall trend in the city remained stagnant. Some goods saw prices surge due to supply shortages, while others experienced a decline due to oversupply. The main items are detailed below:

Sixty-Pound Tinplate Massively Out of Stock: Sixty-pound tinplate is a crucial raw material for can factories. Recently, the market has experienced a severe shortage, and the efforts of various trading guilds to import more are still underway. This has fueled market speculation and soaring prices, with each box reaching fifty taels, a sharp increase of six and a half taels compared to the previous price. Considering the current environment, it is feared that the price trend may continue to rise.

French Wire Nails Enter a State of Decline: After the cessation of eastern goods arriving in Shanghai, the local market initially showed signs of progress for French wire nails. However, sales from customer trading guilds have been affected by warfare, banditry, floods, and communist disturbances, leading to a significant drop in demand. Despite the efforts of various firms to promote sales, they have been unable to reverse the situation. Furthermore, local factories are producing large quantities of nails, causing the entire city to fall into a state of decline. Although the current asking price is only eight taels and seven mace and five candareens, there are still no buyers.

Wang Rongbao Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday 160

Paid a Formal Visit to the Minister of Foreign Affairs This Morning

The Responsibility for the Korean Incident Lies Entirely with Japan

No Word Yet of a Joint Investigation

Wang Rongbao, the Minister to Japan, arrived in Shanghai around 5 PM yesterday on the Taikoo Company's ship Tongzhou from Tianjin. He was accompanied by his staff member, Ren Jiafeng. Due to the fatigue of the journey, he rested in Shanghai overnight and is scheduled to take the express train to Beijing this morning to report to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on the truth of the tragic anti-Chinese case in Korea, discuss response measures, and determine negotiation strategies. A reporter from this newspaper interviewed Mr. Wang at his lodging yesterday. According to him, he was instructed by the Ministry to go to Pyongyang, Incheon, Seoul, and other places to investigate the truth of the Korean incident. The investigation results have been compiled into a complete written report, which has been presented to the Ministry as a basis for negotiation. As for his personal opinions and a brief overview of the Korean incident investigation, he has already detailed them in his previous talks with the press in Liaoning and Tianjin, so he will not repeat them here. In short, this Korean incident was a simultaneous anti-Chinese riot in various parts of Korea. Pyongyang suffered the most severe losses. The total material losses are estimated at 2.43 million Japanese yen, equivalent to about 5 million Chinese yuan. The entire Korean peninsula is under Japanese influence. The Japanese side neither prevented the incident beforehand nor provided protection afterward, so the responsibility cannot be shirked in any way. There has been no word of a joint Chinese-Japanese investigation. He met with Deputy Commander Zhang in Pyongyang and reported everything. He left Tianjin one day and took the Tongzhou ship south, spending five days on the ship. The weather was hot, and he was sweating profusely, making the journey extremely uncomfortable. He will rest here tonight (last night) and go to Beijing tomorrow morning (today) to meet with Foreign Minister Wang in person and report in detail. As for how long he will stay in Beijing and whether he will return to his post, he will completely obey the Central Government's orders. When he was in Korea, many intellectuals from the Korean community came to request an audience and expressed that the Korean incident was not the original intention of the Korean people and asked for forgiveness, expressing extreme remorse. The Japanese authorities also repeatedly stated and guaranteed that such incidents would not happen again. He responded that this was not a personal matter but a matter for the entire Chinese nation.

Another report states that the only reason the Japanese side considers a joint Chinese-Japanese investigation of the Korean incident to be unfavorable is that a joint investigation would naturally lead to the issue of responsibility. Responsibility would require compensation for losses. The Japanese side has repeatedly expressed its willingness to provide full compensation but does not want to bear the name of compensation, otherwise, the current cabinet would not be able to stand, and the Seiyukai party would take its place. However, our side will naturally insist on the three principles of apology, guarantee, and compensation in the negotiation of the Korean incident.

Attention from All Sectors

The Theory of Extending Concessions 161

Foreign Newspapers Have Something to Say

All Sectors Denounce it as Fabrication

The Authorities Consider it a Rumor

Regarding the incident of ignorant merchants in Western Shanghai recklessly requesting the extension of concessions, this newspaper has already reprinted the report from the Shanghai Evening Post in yesterday's newspaper to alert people in Shanghai. However, the Shanghai Evening Post again published the Bureau of Public Roads' reply to the merchants' letter yesterday, still not admitting it was fabricated. The reporter earnestly hopes that merchants in Western Shanghai should immediately make a statement on their own initiative, the General Chamber of Commerce should send someone to investigate the truth as soon as possible, the municipal authorities should actively promote municipal construction, and the diplomatic authorities should make efforts to recover the concessions. Then, this kind of rumor will naturally disappear without being refuted. The various pieces of information obtained yesterday are recorded below.

The wording of the Bureau of Public Roads' reply: According to the report in the Shanghai Evening Post, the Bureau of Public Roads replied to the merchants yesterday (4th), saying that the Bureau of Public Roads is well aware that the situation of the various roads mentioned is unsatisfactory, but until an agreement has been reached with the Shanghai Municipal Government on the issue of roads outside the concessions, the Bureau cannot take any action. According to a member of the Bureau of Public Roads, the merchants of Western Shanghai, or anyone else, believe that the Bureau of Public Roads can take over the roads outside the concessions without the full consent of the Chinese authorities, which is a big mistake.

Declaration of the Third District Party Department: The Third District Party Department issued a declaration yesterday, stating, "Having read the newspaper report that there are unconscionable Chinese people willing to be foreign slaves, requesting the Bureau of Public Roads to extend the concessions and lay asphalt roads, add street lights, and lay streetcars in the three places of Zhujia Gua, Wangjialou, and Shengjiaqiao in Western Shanghai, the establishment of concessions is only for foreign merchants to live in important commercial ports, sovereignty and all administration originally belonged to our country. Later, due to the ignorance of officials in the Qing Dynasty, they abandoned the right to manage, so foreigners took the opportunity to invade, creating today's situation. Fortunately, Mr. Sun Yat-sen, the foresighted and enlightened leader of our party, traveled around to promote and publicize, and the people of the whole country suddenly realized and unanimously worked hard for the movement to recover the concessions. After the National Revolutionary Army took an oath to launch the Northern Expedition and unified the country, it has successively recovered the British and Belgian concessions in Hankou, Zhenjiang, Xiamen, Tianjin, and other places. Our party is taking a further step and actively seeking to recover the concessions in all parts of the country. In this unanimous national effort to abolish consular jurisdiction and recover the concessions, the strange thing of ignorant citizens of China who are unconscionable are requesting the extension of the concessions has occurred. There is no definite evidence, and this news comes from the Shanghai Evening Post, which is run by American imperialists, and it is self-evident that it is intentionally fabricated. It is hoped that our compatriots across the country will pay attention and correct it together. In addition to the people of Western Shanghai making an automatic clarification, they should also be responsible for reporting it. In addition to submitting a letter to the superior government to pay attention to the municipal construction in Western Shanghai and a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to find out the truth as soon as possible, this association hereby makes a solemn declaration.

Citizens Correcting Misconceptions: Citizens Zhou Lianze, Yang Chichan, Yu Xiufang, Li Guohua, Yao Genhuo, Guo Shanqing, Qian Xiuzhai, Jin Xiaodong, Xu Guoying, Liao Changguang, Zheng Jiyu, Ye Nai, Xie Jinrong, Xia Renqi, Hang Wujiu, Xu Ziqing, and more than sixty others, in view of the fact that yesterday's Shen Bao local news column contained a piece entitled "Strange! Chinese People Request the Extension of Concessions," the fact is that the Shanghai Evening Post reported that merchants in Zhujiaqiao, Wangjialou, and Shengjiaqiao in Western Shanghai jointly requested the Bureau of Public Roads to extend the concessions and start construction projects such as roads, street lights, and tap water in the three places to meet the needs of the residents there. They believe that the Shanghai Evening Post fabricated the facts and issued a declaration to correct them. The full text is recorded below: The National News Agency forwarded to various newspapers for the public to read: At a time when the citizens of the whole country are unanimously demanding the recovery of concessions from various countries, the Shanghai Evening Post, run by American imperialists in Shanghai, actually published news that merchants in Zhujiaqiao, Wangjialou, Shengjiaqiao, and other three places in Western Shanghai jointly requested the Bureau of Public Roads to extend the concessions. The newspaper gave this a large headline, saying it with certainty, as if it were true, as if there were people who wanted the concessions to continue to exist, even to expand their scope, and who were willing to bow their heads under the rule of American imperialism and live the life of subjugated slaves. This can be described as farcical and absurd to the extreme. Although the Chinese national character has always been known for peace, and peace is spoken of to the world everywhere, since the revolution to this day, the sinister face and poisonous heart of imperialism have been thoroughly understood, and the movement for national equality has been actively engaged in. The power of concession rule, which should not exist within our territory, should be recovered as soon as possible, and a completely autonomous and independent country should be achieved. This has become the unanimous demand of the whole country, and although this demand has not been fully achieved, it is only a matter of time. However, we can be sure that there are no people who are so willing to betray their country and lose their minds as to have such an absurd and unparalleled act. It is obvious that the Shanghai Evening Post fabricated the facts, trying to extend the life of the concessions and realize its policy in the Far East. Its despicable psychology of struggling to survive when it is at the end of its rope is even more exposed. Fellow merchants in the three places of Zhujiaqiao and others in Western Shanghai should know that if they think that the construction of all road administration, public security, and other undertakings in various places in Western Shanghai is urgent and cannot be delayed, they can ask the municipal authorities to take full responsibility for it. As for what is published in the Shanghai Evening Post, which is close to insulting, they should take the initiative to make a statement, so that it will not be spread abroad, ridiculed by the world, bring shame to the whole body, and be a great obstacle to the recovery of the concessions. On the one hand, it is also to expose the conspiracies of American imperialism. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce, as the leading organization of the merchants of the whole city, should immediately send someone to thoroughly investigate the truth of the matter and announce it to the citizens, so that the public will not be misled by false statements. It is also hoped that the diplomatic authorities will actively work hard to recover the concessions, and the problems of road construction beyond the concessions and public security and municipal administration will be solved easily, so that the imperialists will have no way to covet it and will only speed up their own demise. The country is in a difficult situation, and rumors are alarming. It is hoped that everyone will rise up to correct them. This is a declaration, and we hope you will all be aware of it.

Yu Hongjun Believes it is a Rumor: The news that the Shanghai Evening Post previously reported that merchants in Caojiadu and Shengjiaqiao in Western Shanghai jointly requested the Bureau of Public Roads to extend the concessions is particularly shocking. A reporter from the New Voice Society visited Mr. Yu Hongjun, Secretary-General of the Municipal Government, yesterday to ask whether the news was true or contained poisonous propaganda. He replied that the municipal government also only saw the news in the newspaper and had not received any reports from other sources. At the same time, he believed that the news was an extremely unconscious act, because at a time when the municipal government is working hard to negotiate the construction of roads beyond the concessions and when the Chinese people are vigorously advocating the recovery of the concessions, even if the merchants are greedy for profit and forget their righteousness, they would never dare to do such a great injustice to the world and do something that sells out the country for glory. Even on the foreign side, if they have a little common sense, they would not violate public reason and act rashly. Moreover, judging from the current situation, what foreigners are urgently planning for themselves is a kind of conservatism, because what foreigners are most afraid of and pay attention to now is our country's movement to recover the concessions, fearing that the deep-rooted concession rights that have been obtained will be eradicated at once. In short, what foreigners are now struggling to maintain is their acquired rights, and there is no mention of the word "extension" at all. To reiterate in regard to the merchants' request to extend the concessions, I ask in what name, what qualifications, and in what way can a group of merchants rashly do this? Therefore, we can only regard this propaganda as meddling for no reason and too ignorant. In terms of its content, it is not worth laughing at.

Today

Registration Deadline for Japanese Goods 162

Overdue goods will be treated as smuggled goods.

All confiscated goods will be confiscated.

The registration of Japanese goods by the Anti-Japanese and Aid-Korea Committee and the registration of Japanese goods in member stores by the Municipal Chamber of Commerce will both end today. In the past two days, people who went to the two associations to obtain registration forms almost broke down the door. It is reported that the deadline for registration was decided by the executive committee of the Anti-Japanese Association and the temporary meeting of members of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, and there will be no further extensions. Currently, registration is only today, and goods will be treated as smuggled goods after the deadline, and all confiscated goods will be confiscated.

Shipping News in the Midst of the Boycott 163

Soybeans and Sorghum Converted to Chinese Ships: A large amount of soybeans and sorghum bean cakes in Eastern Provinces are transported to foreign countries and southern Chinese ports every year, and about eight-tenths of them are carried by Japanese ships. Dalian Steamship Company has even built eight special ships this year, preparing to sail from Andong Yingkou, Dalian to southern Chinese ports and other ports, and there is no hope for Chinese ships to get involved. Since the boycott began, Dalian merchants have also decided not to use Japanese ships to transport goods. They have been sending telegrams to Shanghai for several days, asking Shanghai's shipping bureaus to send more Chinese ships to Dalian to carry miscellaneous grains to Shantou, Xiamen, and other places. China Merchants Bureau has already transferred two ships to go, and Zhengji Zhaoxing and others have also sent a large number of ships to carry them. The cargo that was carried by Japanese ships has been completely unloaded.

Chinese People Going to Japan Change to Foreign Ships: There is only one Japanese company, Nippon Yusen Kaisha (NYK), on the Shanghai-Japan route, which has special liner services, so NYK has a monopoly on the transportation of Japanese goods and Chinese people going to Japan. According to NYK, there are eight NYK ships on the China-Japan route, which regularly travel between Osaka, Kobe, Nagoya, and Yokohama. Chinese passengers account for 70-80% of the passengers. Since the boycott began, according to NYK, Chinese people have completely disappeared from the first-class cabins of the company's ships. Even the third-class passengers, who used to travel in groups of dozens, now only have a few. It is said that recently, Chinese people have changed to British and American mail ships.

Japanese Goods in All Warehouses Completely Cleared Out: Before the boycott, the warehouses at the docks of Japanese ships were all full of goods, because after the price of gold rose, those who had ordered goods were unwilling to take delivery. Since the boycott began, Japanese goods stored in the warehouses have been emptied in a week. During the rush to load, NYK alone received 50,000 taels of warehouse rent per day (usually only a little less than 1,000 taels). Recently, there are no Japanese goods in the warehouses of Japanese merchants, and Chinese merchants in Shanghai who have ordered Japanese goods but have not yet been shipped have now cancelled their orders. In recent days, the amount of goods imported from Japan to Shanghai has been greatly reduced. According to Japanese shipping companies, Japanese exporters, in view of the intensity of boycotts in various places, even if they have goods to ship to Shanghai, it is difficult to ship them to various places for sale, so they plan to suspend loading in August and September.

Announcement by the Anti-Japanese Association

Procedures for Inspecting Japanese Goods 164

Inspectors Wear Badges

Those without badges are imposters

The Shanghai Anti-Japanese and Aid-Korea Committee issued its ninth announcement yesterday, stating, "Our association's cargo inspection work has been implemented for many days. We are now afraid that someone will use our association's name to swindle and deceive, so we are specifically announcing the procedures for cargo inspection by the inspectors of the Inspection Section of our association and the addresses of the inspection offices in each district for public inspection. (1) All inspectors of our association wear temporary badges of our association, indicating their name and number, and affixed with the seal of our association (formal badges will be issued in the future and photos will be attached to prevent impersonation). (2) Inspectors of our association are led by a captain during working hours. (3) When our association seizes Japanese goods, it will issue a receipt to the owner of the goods, with the seal of our association and the signature or seal of the director and deputy director and inspectors of each district inspection office. (4) The addresses of the inspection offices in each district of our association are listed below: (A) Zhabei District Inspection Office, No. 100 Xibaoxing Lane, Baoshan Road West; (B) Nanshi District Inspection Office, Pharmaceutical Industry Union inside Dadongmen; (C) Pudong District Inspection District, inside the British-American Tobacco Company's Workers' Children's School, Lan Nidu, Pudong; (D) Huxi Inspection Office, Caojiadu Wujiaochang, No. 9 Bailinan Branch Road. If there are any persons who lack the above procedures or are not dispatched by the above inspection offices and swindle and deceive in the name of the association, all merchants are allowed to immediately take them to the Public Security Bureau for detention in accordance with the law.

Suggestions from Various Industries

Collecting Industrial Funds 165

Raw Materials and Necessities from Japan are Not Boycotted

10% of funds are collected to set up factories.

The Shanghai Cotton Cloth Industry, Silk Satin Industry, Mercerized Cotton Textile Industry, New Drug Industry, Cotton Number Industry, Knitting Industry, North-South Goods Exchange Industry, and more than 30 other trade associations jointly sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, requesting the collection of industrial funds for raw materials and necessities from Japan to prepare for the establishment of factories in order to thoroughly oppose Japan. It reads, "We hereby inform you that this time, the Japanese used Korean people to slaughter overseas Chinese in the Wanbaoshan case, causing heavy casualties. The cruel situation is unprecedented. Compatriots all over the country are deeply aware of the danger of the extinction of the nation and are determined to break the pot and sink the boat and never engage in economic relations with Japan, vowing to fight to the death. If everyone is of one mind and perseveres to the end, the Japanese will eventually soften and beg for mercy. However, our country's industry has always been backward, and its factories are only in their infancy. The raw materials and daily necessities they need, such as fine yarn, coarse yarn, match stems, newspapers, sulfur, pine smoke, rayon, sugar, Japanese coal, cloth, cement, etc., are mostly supplied by other countries, and especially by our eastern neighbor. Now that the whole country is unanimously opposing Japan, if these raw materials and daily necessities are also included in the boycott, then the few factories that we have will inevitably stop production, and the daily necessities used by the people of the country will be cut off. The losses suffered by factory owners have already been huge, and the shortage of livelihood materials for the people has been put aside for the moment. The loss of jobs by workers is enough to create a great terror in society. The actual effect of opposing Japan is still unknown, and the impact on ourselves has already been presented before us. A complete and thorough boycott is a suicidal policy. However, in the world, advantages and disadvantages go hand in hand. If we want the advantages to outweigh the disadvantages, we can only adopt a flexible approach. Before we are able to fully supply ourselves with these raw materials and necessities, we will temporarily not boycott them. However, on the part of those who purchase and transport them, we will collect an industrial fund equal to 10% of the value before allowing them to pass. Otherwise, if they are detained, they should be dealt with in accordance with the regulations. This fund is to be used exclusively for the establishment of this industry, and it should be properly kept by the representatives of the various industries together with your association. It is not allowed to be used until a considerable amount has been collected to establish the industry. After five years, there will be factories everywhere, and the goods needed will be more than enough to supply ourselves. At that time, when we talk about opposing Japan, there is no need to point and wait for the effect to be seen. Our associations are in the business community and are closely concerned. We have something to say and cannot remain silent. We dare to jointly request your association to investigate the situation, review it and implement it. The future of anti-Japan will be greatly benefited.

Establishment of Committee to Study Sino-Japanese Tariff Rates 167

Six Measures Resolved

Three Standing Committee Members Elected

The Committee to Study the Sino-Japanese Tariff Rate Agreement, having previously appointed fifteen members from various organizations last month, formally established itself yesterday at the Chinese National Products Maintenance Association in Nine Acres (a location in Shanghai), and members were sworn into office. Details are as follows:

Page 14

Attending Committee Members: Ge Tianhao from the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, Wang Jiean from the Chinese National Products Maintenance Association, Wang Xingyi from the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Weaving Association, Shi Yunqing from the Wu County Chamber of Commerce, Zhu Dechao from the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, Liu Zihong from the Shandong Native Place Association in Shanghai, Cao Jingyu, Liu Yufu from the Ramie Cloth Guild, Zhan Zhixuan, Chen Yiting from the Shanghai Citizens' National Products Promotion Association, Zhu Zhenhan from the Shanghai Machine-Made National Products Factory Federation, Xu Hanzhang from the Shanghai Ceramics Association, Yang Yongrun from the Shanghai Embroidery Trade Association, and others.

Meeting Proceedings: As the clock struck four, committee members arrived successively. Wang Xingyi was publicly elected as chairman. After ceremonial formalities, the chairman reported on the previous meeting, and discussion began. Wang Jiean reported on opinions submitted from various parties, including modification suggestions from the Wu County Chamber of Commerce and the Shanghai Woodwork Trade Association. Ballots were then cast to elect three standing committee members, and the following items were resolved:

Standing Committee Member List: Eleven individuals voted in the election. The Shanghai Silk Trade representative was absent due to business. The results revealed that Wang Jiean received eleven votes, Wang Xingyi received nine votes, and Ge Tianhao received six votes. They were elected as standing committee members.

Oath of Office: "I swear with utmost sincerity to serve as a member of the Committee to Study the Sino-Japanese Tariff Rate Agreement. I will uphold impartiality, conduct thorough research on equal Sino-Japanese tariff rates, seek benefits for national products, and fulfill my civic duty. I hereby swear."

Key Resolutions: (1) Send letters to Chinese chambers of commerce in various locations in Korea, requesting reports on tariff situations over the past decade and soliciting opinions on modifying the Sino-Japanese tariff rates. (2) Send letters to the National Federation of Chambers of Commerce, requesting them to telegraph national chambers of commerce, soliciting opinions on modifying the Sino-Japanese tariff rate agreement and encouraging the free organization of research societies in various localities. (3) Send letters to the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce, requesting them to inform various trade associations to submit written statements on their suffering under unequal Sino-Japanese tariff rates. (4) Commence research upon receiving opinions from all parties and invite legal and tariff experts to participate. (5) Request newspapers to publish news of the committee as much as possible to arouse the attention of all industries. (6) Compile the research results into a book and submit it to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs for consideration.

Chiang Tsun-Kwei Died Yesterday 170

Funeral Tomorrow

Mr. Chiang Tsun-Kwei, an important figure in military and political circles, passed away at 1:50 PM yesterday at his residence at No. 23 Avenue Safoe, French Concession. Details of his illness and a biography of Mr. Chiang are presented below:

Portrait of Mr. Chiang Tsun-Kwei 171

Brief Biography: Chiang, courtesy name Boqi, was 50 years old and a native of Zhuji, Zhejiang Province. He was the son of the renowned Zhejiang literary figure, Mr. Chiang Kwan-Yun. He studied at the Qiushi Academy in Hangzhou from a young age. At the age of 22, he went to Japan to study, entering the Military Academy. He graduated from the first class in the Cavalry Department. He and Chiang Fang-Chen were known as the "Two Chiangs of Zhejiang." After returning to China, he served in the Qing army. During the Xinhai Revolution, he served as Military Governor of the Guangdong and Zhejiang armies, a member of the Political Conference, and a senator in the Senate. In 1920, he entered the Guangdong military government and served as Deputy Chief of Staff. In 1923, when Sun Yat-sen returned to Guangdong, he again served as Deputy Minister of the Military Affairs Department. In 1926, after the Northern Expedition secured Shanghai, he was appointed Chairman of the Shanghai Political Branch, concurrently serving on the Zhejiang Provincial Committee, as Senior Advisor to the Commander-in-Chief, and as a member of the Relief Committee. He then came to Shanghai to recuperate, residing at No. 23 Avenue Safoe, French Concession. He spent his days chanting scriptures and assisting in all charitable endeavors, without concerning himself with current affairs.

Death: Mr. Chiang, due to practicing equestrian shooting, suffered from stomach ailments that recurred periodically. After being stimulated last year, he contracted heart disease. His condition suddenly worsened on the fourth day of the fifth lunar month this year, with constant vomiting, consuming only thin porridge. He consulted Dr. Lu Zhong'an, a traditional Chinese medicine practitioner, with no improvement. On the 23rd of last month, he entered the Sino-Western Sanitarium on Xipushi Road, consulting Dr. Langban, a Western doctor, also without success. On the 1st of this month, his condition suddenly changed. That afternoon, he was moved back to his residence. At 10 AM on the 2nd, he briefly stopped breathing, but recovered at 3 PM. His family was overjoyed, but he was delirious, repeatedly asking for cold drinks, which his family dared not give him. He passed away at 1:50 PM yesterday afternoon, leaving behind two sons and two daughters. The eldest son, Yimen, is 18 years old, and the second son, Shuanglong, is four years old. The eldest daughter, Dongrong, and the second daughter, Donghua, are both studying at Fudan Vocational High School, except for Shuanglong. Mr. Chiang's remains are scheduled to be placed in a coffin at his residence tomorrow.

Death of Taiwanese Revolutionary Leader 172

Local Taiwanese Compatriots Preparing Memorial Service

Mr. Chiang Wei-Shui, a leader of the Taiwanese revolution, suddenly died of typhoid fever at the Taipei Hospital yesterday morning. All who heard the news were overcome with grief. Mr. Chiang was a key member of the Taiwanese People's Party. For decades, he tirelessly led the Taiwanese people's liberation movement. He pursued the revolution without fear of violence, incurring the Japanese authorities' animosity. He was arrested and detained countless times. In modern Taiwanese revolutionary history, Mr. Chiang participated in almost every event. In 1919, Mr. Chiang initiated the organization of liberation groups and the Taiwan Cultural Association in Taiwan, disregarding personal safety and openly resisting the Japanese's various unreasonable oppressions, while publicizing the Japanese's political, economic, and cultural invasion schemes abroad. He was a pioneer for the passionate young people of Taiwan. His sudden passing is a great misfortune for the oppressed peoples of East Asia. Upon receiving the news yesterday, local Taiwanese compatriots convened an emergency meeting that evening to prepare for a memorial service to be held in Shanghai soon, and a preparatory office was established at the Overseas Chinese Hospital at Bowling Green Road.

Successful Conclusion of Shaanxi Disaster Relief 173

Relief Funds Revenue and Expenditure Audited and Certified by Accountants

Details of Distribution Reported to Shanghai by Zhu Qinglan

The Shanghai Temporary Urgent Disaster Relief Committee for Shaanxi, which had been operating for two and a half months, collected over 431,000 yuan in relief funds, in addition to numerous relief goods not included in the amount. All funds and goods were successively transported to Xi'an and handed over to Zhu Qinglan, head of the North China Philanthropic Federation, for personal distribution. The committee then concluded its affairs, gathered all donation lists, account books, and remittance receipts, and entrusted accountant Xu Yongzuo to prepare a report to be submitted to the committee. The report included a statement from the accountant certifying that the attached revenue and expenditure statement was accurately prepared based on the records and that the revenue and expenditure items listed therein accurately reflected the association's true revenue and expenditure situation regarding relief funds during the stated period. Zhu's telegrams detailing the emergency relief distributed to various counties in Shaanxi, as well as work relief for water conservancy, burial assistance, purchase of cattle, well drilling, and subsidies to disaster relief orphanages, have also been mailed to Shanghai. It is reported that the committee will publish these details in the newspaper soon to reassure the generous donors who contributed to disaster relief. The committee's efficient operations and complete procedures set a rare standard for disaster relief efforts.

Disaster Relief Committee Suggests Borrowing Rent from the City 174

The Municipal Government Expresses Disapproval

Since the floods occurred in various places, the Capital Disaster Relief Committee proposed borrowing rent from the city to relieve the suffering of the people. However, according to the municipal government yesterday, although borrowing rent was implemented once during the campaign against Feng Yuxiang, it was done out of necessity due to military tension and the Ministry of Finance had previously consulted with Shanghai's banking and money industries. Therefore, it was reluctantly done to suppress rebellion and quell internal strife for the sake of the nation, but the method was not appropriate. The Chinese area is currently hoping to build houses and develop the city, so that future construction can compete with the concessions and correct the erroneous perceptions of citizens. If repeated disturbances are added, homeowners will be afraid to move forward, which will contradict the purpose of developing the city in the Chinese area. However, relieving disaster victims is also an urgent matter, but other methods should be used and not rent.

Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association

Continued Receipt of Letters and Telegrams from Provinces Requesting Relief 175

The Shanghai Chinese and Foreign Charity Relief Association received an urgent telegram from the Party Affairs Rectification Committee of Huangchuan County, Henan, stating: "Huangchuan County has repeatedly suffered from banditry, and the people are unable to bear their lives. Unexpectedly, disaster has struck again. On June 18, heavy rain poured down for days, causing mountain floods to rage and waves to surge. As far as the eye can see, the villages and fields have become a swamp. Houses have been submerged, and crops have been washed away. Countless residents have perished in the waves. Now, their homes have been reduced to nothing, and their fields have turned into mud. The disaster victims have nowhere to live and are camping in the open, their cries echoing through the wilderness. Witnessing this tragedy, our committee proposes disaster relief, but due to limited financial resources, we hereby telegraph, requesting the party and country's virtuous leaders, benevolent people, and righteous individuals to generously provide assistance to save these survivors." They also received a telegram from various organs and organizations in Hefei County, Anhui, stating: "Hefei is unfortunately stricken by a sudden mountain flood, turning the county seat into a swamp. The embankments have all been destroyed, and crops and houses have been washed away without a trace. Deaths of people and livestock are too numerous to count. This catastrophic disaster is rare in a century. In addition to organizing a disaster relief fundraising committee, we humbly request your assistance to avert this catastrophe." They also received an urgent telegram from the Disaster Relief Branch Association of Taixing County, Jiangsu, stating: "Taixing County has been inundated with three days of heavy rain since the 4th of this month, turning the fields into swamps. Unexpectedly, on the 11th, a hurricane struck again, and the floodwaters deepened, making drainage difficult, resulting in a vast expanse of water. Collapsed houses and injured people are frequently reported. Currently, the entire county is almost completely submerged in floodwaters. The disaster is of unprecedented magnitude in decades. Future food supplies are a cause for concern, and how to maintain the current situation is an urgent matter. We earnestly request immediate relief." They also received an urgent telegram from the Kuomintang Executive Committee of Gaoyou County, Jiangsu, stating: "Since the summer, our county has been ravaged by continuous rain, coupled with the overflowing of the Huai, Yi, and Si rivers and the surge of the Yangtze River tide. The water level in the rivers and lakes is rising rapidly. Fields and crops have been submerged, and disaster victims are everywhere. The disaster is severe, and the situation is perilous. All disaster victims in the county are clamoring for food. We hereby appeal for immediate relief to aid the disaster victims." They also received a telegram from the Hubei Flood Relief Association stating: "Hubei Province has experienced continuous heavy rain, causing the Yangtze and Han rivers to swell. Many embankments along both banks have collapsed, and the residents of the three towns have suffered a major catastrophe. The dire situation is difficult to describe fully. However, the disaster area is too large, and relief is urgently needed. We hope you will raise your voice and lend a helping hand. May benevolent and righteous people provide a continuous stream of aid." They also received an urgent telegram from various organizations in Tongling County, Anhui, stating: "Tongling is located near the Yangtze River and has a low-lying terrain. Since spring and summer, there has been continuous rain, causing mountain floods to break through all embankments. Fields, livestock, and houses have been lost, and those displaced are crying to the heavens. They are exposed to the wind and eat in the open, which is unbearable to witness. Now, the autumn harvest is hopeless, and the supply of firewood and rice has been cut off. The hardship has reached its peak. We urgently request immediate relief to save lives."

The Entertainment Industry Enthusiastically Raises Funds for Disaster Victims 176

The Cantonese opera troupe "Yong Shou Nian Ban," featuring Bai Yutang, Qianli Ju, and Li Yunnong, has consulted with the Shanghai Performing Arts Federation regarding fundraising methods, considering the recent floods in various provinces. Disaster Relief Requested for Jiangpu and Other Counties 177

Disaster Reports Received by the Ji Sheng Association

The China Ji Sheng Association reported that various legal organizations in Jiangpu County, Jiangsu, stated: "Jiangpu County, bordering the Yangtze River to the front and Anhui Province to the rear, has been plagued by rain for a month, resulting in mountain floods. In the northern area, most of the polders have been breached, and countless people have been swept away. On the 23rd and 24th of last month, torrential rain poured down day and night, coupled with the overflow of the Yellow Mountain flood for 800 miles in northern Anhui, which flowed straight down. All polder embankments were breached. Even villages and towns on flat ground, such as Chahe, Dongge, Yongning, and Tangquan, were submerged in several feet of water, causing the Jinpu Railway to be washed away for more than ten miles, suspending train service for about four or five days. The entire area was a vast expanse of water without boundaries. People, livestock, and objects were swept away without a trace. Disaster victims who climbed trees were rescued by the urgent relief association, while no fewer than several thousand people took their families and sought refuge in the mountains, exposed to the wind and rain, crying for food. Due to the turbulent floodwaters, those who failed to escape in time drowned in large numbers. The magnitude of this catastrophe is unprecedented. They have dispatched Xu Rangsan and Gu Laixi to report the disaster to the provincial and Shanghai authorities, calling for prompt relief to save lives." They have also received reports from more than ten counties, including Taixing, Wujin, Jiangning, and Huaiyin, regarding the disaster situation, which are similar in essence. Some report that the people are destitute and awaiting rescue from the ditches, while others report that agriculture has been devastated and they hope to alleviate the great suffering of hunger. The cries of disaster victims are everywhere, and the number of dead and wounded is unprecedented in hundreds of years, making it a catastrophe for hundreds of millions of people. Their voices are hoarse and painful, and they have no tears to shed. They ask for a drop of Yangzhi (compassion) to be the savior of thousands of families. Those with a heart to save the world should seize this opportunity to do immeasurable good. Let generous aid flow continuously and in abundance. We look forward to it."

Relief for Natural and Man-Made Disasters in Jiangxi 178

The Province Divided into Nine Zones

The Chinese Red Cross Society received a telegram from special investigators Wu Jiasan and Wei Keqiang, who were dispatched to investigate the disaster situation: "The communist bandits in Jiangxi Province are gradually being suppressed. The Party and Government Committee has divided the disaster area into nine zones, establishing a sub-association with a director in each zone, overseeing several counties, to handle various party, government, and relief matters. The first zone includes Xiushui, Wuning, Yifeng, and Tonggu; the second zone includes Pingxiang, Wanzai, Yichun, and Fenyi; the third zone includes Yongxin, Anfu, Lianhua, Ningguo, and Suichuan; the fourth zone includes Jian, Yongfeng, Jishui, Wan'an, and Taihe; the fifth zone includes Ganxian, Yundu, Xingguo, Nankang, and Xinfeng; the sixth zone includes Guangchang, Ningdu, Shicheng, and Ruijin; the seventh zone includes Nanfeng, Yihuang, Le'an, Nancheng, and Lichuan; the eighth zone includes Jinxi, Guixi, Yujiang, Zixi; the ninth zone includes Shangrao, Yiyang, Yushan, Guangfeng, Dexing, Hengfeng, and Qianshan. Almost every county in the nine zones has suffered, but the sixth zone is the most severely affected, followed by the third, eighth, and seventh zones. Yesterday, we met with Commander Xiong Tianyi and Chief Wen Shaoyun, who agreed to allocate 5,000 yuan from the relief funds allocated by our association to the fifth zone, which has just been cleared of bandits, where disaster victims are gathered and clamoring for food, as emergency relief to prevent starvation. This is only a temporary measure to address the immediate needs and is not enough to be universally distributed. The entire province is paralyzed, and people are in dire straits, awaiting rescue. Commander Wen and Chief Wen deeply hope that charitable organizations in Shanghai will follow Article 8 of the Jiangxi Province relief regulations, which states that for counties with deep disasters, no income, and no ability to raise funds, charitable organizations should discuss bringing funds and personnel to manage the relief in a county or several counties, providing emergency relief to save tens of millions of dying disaster victims. Please dispatch personnel to Jiangxi as soon as possible to engage in disaster relief in a county or several counties, or designate several counties to provide emergency relief to save tens of millions of dying disaster victims. Jiangxi Province has been ravaged by both communist bandits and continuous rain, resulting in a severe flood disaster. The disaster situation is extremely serious, and it is necessary to raise a large amount of funds to alleviate this catastrophe. As for designating counties for relief, please submit it to the Standing Committee for review and resolution. Raising relief funds is a matter of utmost urgency. We urge you to broadly solicit donations to save these survivors. We cannot express enough our plea on behalf of the people in this telegram. Secretary Wei Keqiang, Advisor Wu Jiasan."

The Printing Industry Resumes Operations Today 179

Labor and Management Listen to the Mediation of the Bureau of Social Affairs

Treatment Conditions Will Be Discussed at Mediation

After the printing industry in the city went on strike, the Bureau of Social Affairs first summoned representatives from both sides for questioning yesterday afternoon to facilitate mediation. Qu Shou Kang and Xia Hailin represented the Printing Industry Workers' Union, while Dai Zhong Lin, He Zhijin, Chen Bing Xi, and Jin Shun Qing represented the Printing Industry Guild. Lu Yin Chu represented the City Party Headquarters. Zhang Shuye of the Bureau of Social Affairs questioned the parties, and Wang Zhiqin took notes. The guild representatives insisted on a nine-hour workday. Both sides held their ground, arguing fiercely. Zhang Shuye advised both sides to resume work first and temporarily maintain the nine-hour workday while awaiting lawful mediation. If an eight-hour workday is prescribed in the future, overtime wages can be paid for the extra hour worked. The treatment conditions will be discussed when the mediation committee is formally convened. The labor representatives accepted the advice and agreed to return to the union to discuss it with the workers before making a decision. They then notified the members to temporarily resume work as usual.

French Concession

Two Courts Officially Open This Morning 180

The Third Branch of the Jiangsu High Court and the Shanghai Second Special District District Court have largely completed their internal organization since their establishment. Besides emergency cases, which were tried once a few days ago, the courts continued to hear four emergency cases yesterday. From 3:15 PM to 5:15 PM, the Second Special District District Court held its first court affairs meeting to properly distribute various tasks. The courts are scheduled to officially open this morning around 10:00 AM to hear new and old civil and criminal cases. At the same time, they will officially begin accepting litigation documents. News from yesterday is recorded below:

Continued Hearing of Urgent Cases: Yesterday morning, the French Concession police department delivered three urgent criminal cases to the Second Special District District Court, including cases of fighting, counterfeiting trademarks, and prostitutes soliciting customers. The trademark counterfeiting case was an old case. Because the suspect is currently in custody, the police department was allowed to deliver the case for trial on the originally scheduled continuation date. Only one case requiring transfer was received in the afternoon. All cases were heard by Criminal Division Chief Ge Zhi Qin. The three cases in the morning were heard from 10:30 AM to 12:30 PM, and the case in the afternoon was heard from approximately 3:00 PM to 3:30 PM. All cases were adjourned for further hearing.

Court Affairs Meeting: Yesterday afternoon at 3:15 PM, the President of the Second Special District District Court, Ying Shi, convened the first court affairs meeting with the division chiefs and judges. Attendees included President Ying Shi, Civil Division judges Pang Shurong and Qu Zengze, Criminal Division judges Luo Renji and Xiong Huiping, Civil Summary Court judge Zhu Ganlin, Criminal Summary Court judge Wu Fanglian, and Criminal Division Chief Ge Zhi Qin (who joined after hearing cases), totaling eight people. The discussion lasted approximately two hours, ending at 5:15 PM. It is reported that the work of civil and criminal matters has been properly distributed and that the document section has created a list so that they can begin processing the work today.

Official Opening: The official opening is scheduled to begin around 10:00 AM this morning. Because the French police department cannot deliver the cases in time, it cannot be any earlier. The cases to be heard first have not yet been determined because the French side has not provided the registry after receiving the old cases. Therefore, it is not yet possible to decide. The official opening today will only hear new cases and old cases that are scheduled for continuation today. All old civil and criminal cases that do not have a scheduled continuation date and must be heard by the District Court must wait until the registry is received from the French side, sorted by type, and then summoned for hearing. It is expected to take another week from today.

Prison Repairs: After the judicial police officers of the French side guarding the prison handed over their duties last time, they dismantled or removed many of the original firefighting equipment, prisoner washing equipment, and other miscellaneous items in the prison before they left. The Chief Clerk of the Second Special District District Court, Xiao Quanfang, negotiated with French Consul General Canglin on behalf of the court. The French Consul General formally replied to Xiao yesterday afternoon that he agreed to repair them according to the number and set an engineer to investigate and deal with it today.

Permission to Appeal: In the last few days before the French Tribunal was handed over, it hastily judged many civil and criminal cases, resulting in a large number of dissatisfied parties. According to the Chief Clerk Xiao Jinfang's statement regarding this type of case, these cases should be enforced according to the adjudication according to the agreement terms. However, those who believe that the adjudication is unfair and express their dissatisfaction can appeal to the Third Branch of the High Court within fifteen days of the adjudication. The High Court will accept the appeal in order to resolve the issue fairly.

Zhu and Gong Go to Qingdao: Former French Tribunal Judges Zhu Qi and Gong Xiang did not retain their positions after the Tribunal was reorganized by our country's Ministry of Justice. Therefore, they took a company steamer with their families to Qingdao yesterday.

Measures for Increased Fees for Foreign Ship Pilots 181

Last month, the pilots of foreign ships in the city went on strike to demand higher fees, lasting for a week. After mediation by the Director of the Jianghai Customs Port Authority, they resumed work first, with a two-week deadline for the shipping companies to decide whether to increase fees and reply to the Pilots' Association. This matter has been reported in this newspaper several times. On the 4th of this month, the two-week deadline expired. The reporter made thorough inquiries into the situation and recorded what he heard below:

Temporary No Fee Increase: Since the pilots resumed work on July 22, the foreign ships in Shanghai have convened several meetings to discuss the matter. The majority of the companies concluded that they should maintain the old rules and not advocate for higher fees. The shipping companies believe that they already bear a large amount of pilotage fees and that maritime transport business has been declining recently. Therefore, they decided to take a calm attitude towards the issue. Ships will continue to enter and exit the port according to the old rules, and the shipping companies will not respond to the Pilots' Association, leaving the matter unresolved. Therefore, there has been no expression recently.

Shortened Pilotage Line: After the Port Director's mediation, the shipping companies telegraphed their respective headquarters to report on the progress and request instructions regarding the fee increase. During these two weeks, the shipping companies consulted back and forth on this matter more than once. It is said that the ship owners unanimously opposed the increase in pilotage fees and, as a precaution, the shipping companies negotiated with the captains of ships sailing to the Far East. In the event that the pilots insist on raising fees, the shipping companies can also accommodate it, but on the condition that the pilotage line is shortened. In the past, foreign ships coming to Shanghai had to engage a pilot from Tongsha to Wu Song, and then take them into the Huangpu River. The same was true for ships leaving the port. The sea route was very long and required two sets of fees. Now, it will be changed so that ships travel on their own from Tongsha to Wu Song (the ship owners and chief mates are familiar with this section), and then engage a pilot at the mouth of Wu Song to guide them in. In this way, 4/5ths of the pilotage sea route can be reduced, and the ships will only have to pay for a short section of pilotage. Even if they fully accept the association's demands, they can actually reduce the cost by 3/5ths. It is understood that the shipping companies have decided to adopt this proposal: if the pilots insist on raising fees, they will shorten the pilotage line. If the pilots shelve the fee increase, they will maintain the original status and not change it for the time being.

Australian Aviator to Pass Through Shanghai 182

The Ta Mei Evening News reports that Australian aviator Bert Hinkler, piloting a small aircraft, departed from Australia, intending to travel via the Philippines, China, Japan, cross the Pacific Ocean to Canada, then cross the Atlantic Ocean to London. Yesterday evening (the 4th), the local Asiatic Petroleum Company received a telegram stating that Hinkler departed from Manila two days ago and arrived at Tamsui in Taiwan. He will now fly from Tamsui to Shanghai, and is expected to arrive in Wusong today (the 5th). However, very little information has been received locally regarding the flight, as Hinkler originally did not plan to pass through China. Later, because the Japanese authorities prohibited him from flying over strategic areas in Taiwan, he temporarily changed his route, hence his flight to Shanghai from Taiwan. It is expected that he will now take a route via Peiping (Beijing) to Japan. The Asiatic Petroleum Company in Shanghai has prepared everything and will proceed to Wusong to welcome him upon receiving his departure telegram. The duration of Hinkler's stay in Shanghai is currently unknown, but it is estimated that he will stay for a day or two.
